Urgent Meeting of Shareholders of Jicheng Pharmacy 169

The Resolution to Resume Business Should Seek Creditors' Consent, If More Than Three-Quarters Agree, Business Will Resume

According to Xinxin News Agency, Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy on Nanjing Road in this city was unable to circulate funds due to the sluggish market and the accumulation of inventory. In addition, depositors went to withdraw deposits one after another, which could not be met. On December 28 of last year, the board of directors of the pharmacy entrusted lawyer Yang Linzhi to temporarily declare a suspension of business. Now it is known that the company convened an emergency shareholders' meeting at No. 40 Ningbo Road at 2 p.m. yesterday, with 56 people including Chu Minyi and Tu Kaizheng attending, with more than three-quarters of the shares. Most of them advocated the resumption of business on the issue of the company's suspension of business. In particular, Mr. Chu Minyi was most concerned about the company's resumption of business. It was said that the new pharmaceutical industry in our country is in a new era of development and should be actively developed, or it may be possible to regain the rights and interests of the pharmaceutical industry. If a Chinese pharmacy goes bankrupt, it will reduce a sales channel, so it is hoped that general creditors will express their consent to the resolution to resume business, and business can resume.

Proposals 170

The proposals of the shareholders' meeting are as follows: (1) Since the company has been unable to circulate funds, it should suspend business. During the suspension period, the board of directors should still seek creditors' consent in accordance with the original reconciliation plan. If more than three-quarters of the creditors express their consent in writing, the company will resume business immediately. (2) If creditors accept half of the company's issuance of priority shares, the company should issue priority shares immediately and apply to the competent authorities for approval in accordance with the law. The rights of the priority shares are subject to the provisions of the original plan. (3) If creditors are unwilling to express their consent before the 25th of this month, or if those who express their consent do not reach more than three-quarters of the amount of debt, the company will be liquidated and liquidated immediately, and accountant Wang Sifang and lawyer Yang Linzhi will be selected as liquidators.

Resumption of Business Methods 171

Yesterday, two resolutions were made on the resumption of business: (1) Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy Co., Ltd. will repay the company's debts in installments of ten years without interest from June 30 of this year. The first repayment period will be on June 30, 1935, and repayments will be made in turn every year on June 30. (2) Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy Co., Ltd. will issue priority shares for half of the company's debts, and is willing to repay the remaining half of the principal in five years in equal installments without interest from June 30 of this year. The first repayment period will be on June 30, 1935, and repayments will be made in turn every year on June 30. (The rights of priority shares are listed below) (1) The annual dividend of priority shares is 6%. (2) If the company has a surplus in its annual business, no ordinary shares may be paid unless the annual dividend of priority shares has been fully paid. (3) If the company is liquidated, all remaining assets will be distributed to priority shares first.

An Earthquake Will Occur in Shanghai Around Noon on the Fifth of Next Month 176

Originating from Crustal Movement

Unrelated to Volcanic Activity

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Xujiahui Observatory in Shanghai reports that an earthquake is expected to occur in Shanghai around noon on February 5th of this year (the second day of the Spring Festival). This earthquake is believed to be caused by movements within the earth's crust and is not specifically related to volcanic activity. It is due to the movement of rocks along fault lines within the crust. Geologists have long asserted that the earth's crust was initially formed by lava, which either solidified or boiled, undergoing repeated changes. The boiling action caused various substances to coalesce, with lighter substances floating and heavier substances sinking. The major continents of the world are generally composed of lighter rocks such as granite. Therefore, it is said that Asia's vast weight and the rock layers at the bottom along the fault lines, due to the influence of pressure, have layers that are nearing decay or have already decayed (decay does not mean pulverization; the bottoms of continents and oceans are connected), causing external pressure to force and compress parts of the internal substance to come closer together, thus causing an earthquake. The seismic waves radiate outward from the epicenter and transmit to the ground.

Ministry of Finance Announces Revised Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax 177

Divided into Three Categories: Tobacco, Alcohol, and Foreign Liquor

Licenses Must Be Obtained Every Quarter, with Severe Penalties for Violations

According to China News Agency, the Ministry of Finance recently revised the provisional regulations for tobacco and alcohol business license taxes and officially announced them for implementation. The business licenses are divided into three categories: tobacco, alcohol, and foreign liquor, and must be obtained quarterly. The types and tax rates are as follows:

Tobacco and Alcohol Licenses 178

(1) Tobacco Business Licenses are divided into wholesale and retail categories. Those who wholesale tobacco products to retail merchants are considered wholesale businesses and are divided into three levels: (A) Branches and distribution offices of cigarette manufacturers pay 100 yuan per quarter; (B) Tobacco shops engaged in wholesale trade pay 40 yuan per quarter; (C) Wholesale shops dealing in various types of tobacco pay 20 yuan per quarter; (D) Other shops mainly dealing in all types of tobacco pay 8 yuan per quarter; (E) Other shops additionally selling all types of tobacco pay 4 yuan per quarter; (F) Tobacco retailers who set up stalls pay 2 yuan per quarter; (G) Itinerant tobacco retailers pay 50 cents per quarter.

(2) Alcohol Business Licenses are divided into wholesale and retail categories. Those who wholesale alcohol products to retail merchants are considered wholesale businesses and are divided into three types: (A) Those who wholesale over 240,000 jin per year pay 32 yuan per quarter; (B) Those who wholesale between 120,000 jin and less than 240,000 jin per year pay 24 yuan per quarter; (C) Those who wholesale between 24,000 jin and less than 120,000 jin per year pay 16 yuan per quarter. Those who retail alcohol to consumers are considered retail businesses and are divided into three levels: (A) Those who open shops selling all types of alcohol pay 8 yuan per quarter; (B) Other shops additionally selling all types of alcohol pay 4 yuan per quarter; (C) Itinerant alcohol retailers pay 50 cents per quarter.

Foreign Liquor Licenses 179

(3) Foreign Liquor Business Licenses are divided into wholesale and retail categories. Wholesale businesses are divided into two levels: (A) Various mechanized wineries, importers, winery branches, and exclusive agents pay 50 yuan per quarter; (B) Various agencies and wholesale foreign liquor stores pay 15 yuan per quarter. Retail businesses are divided into two levels: (A) Various restaurants, hotels, and bars pay 10 yuan per quarter; (B) Various retail foreign liquor stores pay 5 yuan per quarter.

28 Chinese Cotton Mills Petition for the Suppression of Cotton Speculators and Monopolies 180

Seeking to Maintain the Balance of Cotton Yarn Prices

According to Guowen News Agency, 28 Chinese cotton mills, including Wing On and Weaving & Spinning, jointly petitioned the government and the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday, stating: "Petitioning for the suppression of speculators who are destroying real industry, which cannot be delayed. We sincerely request a decisive action to safeguard the national textile industry." The petition stated that cotton has been expensive and yarn has been cheap in recent years, causing cotton mills to suffer losses and lack vitality. However, speculators, knowing that domestic cotton production is insufficient for factory use, continue to raise prices and hoard, resulting in a growing gap between the prices of cotton and yarn at the yarn exchange, preventing a balance. The danger facing the yarn industry cannot be ignored. In all countries with cotton production in the world, the exchange has never simultaneously priced both cotton and yarn, fearing that the disparity in value would hinder the textile industry. However, the Shanghai Chinese Cotton Yarn Exchange is different. Cotton and yarn are auctioned at the same time, with cotton standardized to domestic cotton, allowing speculators to succeed in their monopolistic manipulation. The price of cotton rises higher and higher, while the price of yarn lags behind. According to the current market conversion of cotton bids to yarn prices, each bale of cotton yarn loses more than 20 yuan. For several months, cotton mills across the country have suffered from this situation. Speculators only seek private gain, disregarding the overall situation, knowing that even if the price of raw cotton is raised to an extremely high level, factories cannot stop working; even if the price of yarn is at a huge loss, factories cannot stockpile and not sell. As long as the factories continue to operate, they have to reluctantly buy expensive cotton and sell cheap yarn, facing a dilemma. The life of cotton mills across the country is entirely in the hands of a few organized speculators. The urgency of the matter cannot be overstated. If the government does not provide swift relief, the whole situation will collapse in the near future. Once the opportunity is lost, it will be too late to take remedial measures. Therefore, we sincerely petition your esteemed government to dispatch officials to Shanghai to conduct a thorough investigation of the situation. At the same time, we request that the Chinese Cotton Yarn Exchange be ordered to maintain a balance between the prices of cotton and yarn. If the manufacturing cost of 20-count standard yarn, converted from the market price of 430 jin of standard cotton (excluding taxes), is less than 45 yuan, the auction should be stopped immediately until the market price returns to a reasonable difference. This is an urgent and immediate solution. We earnestly implore you to adopt it and implement it to relieve our predicament. We deeply pray." The petition was presented to the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Shanghai Municipal Government by the following petitioners: Wing On Factories 1, 2, 3, and 4, Weaving & Spinning, Shen Hsin, Heng Feng, Qingdao Huaxin, Xie Feng, Da Tong, Min Feng, Tong Cheng, Yu Feng Su Lun, He Feng, Da Sheng Factories 3 and 1, Three Friends, Min Sheng, Zhen Tai, Bao Xing, Da Cheng, Hong Zhang, Fu An, Pu Yi, Heng Da, Da Feng, and Zhen Hua.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables for Clarification of the Stamp Duty Standards for Three-Part Forms 184

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, on the 11th of this month, we received a letter from the Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Goods Trade Association stating: 'Respectfully, the Guanshengyuan Company informed us that when a transaction is completed at the store's retail section, an invoice is issued in the three-part invoice book, with the first part given to the customer, the second part given to the accounting department for verification, and the third part kept for record. Regarding the method of affixing stamps, it is natural to affix sufficient stamps to the first invoice in accordance with regulations. However, we would like to request your Chamber to forward a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for clarification as to whether stamps should be affixed to the second and third parts and whether stamps should be affixed to the cover of the original invoice book in order to have something to follow.' Based on this, we are hereby forwarding the situation and requesting your esteemed Chamber to promptly review and reply so that we can forward it accordingly. Invoices are issued for the needs of customers, and according to regulations, only one copy is required. The company uses a three-part format for record-keeping purposes. The second and third parts are copies and should not be affixed with stamps. Furthermore, the three-part invoice is bound into a book and covered with a cover. Although the form is similar to accounting books, the effect of the invoice is independent on each page. Therefore, stamps should be affixed to each page individually, which is different from accounting books that use one year as the start and end date and affix stamps to each book. Since stamps are affixed to each page of the issued invoice, there is no need to affix stamps again to the cover. In order to ensure that the methods are consistent, we hereby cable your esteemed Ministry to approve and circulate this for the merchants to follow, which will be convenient for all. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Case of Wu Hua Bank Nears Conclusion 189

Huang Linsheng Appeared in Court to Present the Progress of Liquidation

Zhang Chaozu Repeated the Trial and Arguments Concluded

After the Shanghai branch of Wu Hua Bank, located at 130 Ningbo Road in the Public Concession, and the Eight Immortals Bridge branch in the French Concession simultaneously went bankrupt on August 21st of last year, Zhulonggen, Chen Xianji, Luo Lihua (female), Shi Pengfei, Duzhiji, Shibilong, Shen Peng, Zhou Delin, Wang Fulin, Pan Yuanji, and ten other creditors of the two branches jointly hired lawyers to file a private prosecution in the Criminal Court of the Second Special District District Court, accusing the managers and assistant managers of the two branches of Wu Hua Bank, Fan Shaoliang, Wang Jian'e, Ye Haitian, Wu You, Xie Shunzhi, Tang Songshan, counselors Tang Shoumin, Chen Bingqian, and eight others of breach of trust and fraud, using the advertisement of the five-year and ten-year savings plans to promote the absorption of deposits, and failing to register with the National Government before opening. They requested that the case be investigated and dealt with according to the law. The case was originally heard by Judge Zhang Chaozu. The first hearing was postponed because the defendants had not appeared. Later, Judge Zhang was transferred to the High Branch Court, and Judge Xiong Huiping took over the case. He held two hearings to summon the defendants, who all appeared in court with their defense lawyers. Huang Linsheng, the representative sent by the Guangzhou head office to Shanghai with full authority for liquidation, also appeared in court and stated the progress of the liquidation, stating that the accounting books could be liquidated and compiled in about two weeks for submission to the case, as reported in previous newspapers. Now that Judge Zhang has returned to the Special Second Court, yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang convened both parties to continue the hearing, announced the renewal of the trial, questioned the plaintiffs about the grounds for their prosecution, and the defendants' confessions, which were roughly the same as reported previously and will not be repeated. The court also summoned Huang Linsheng, the representative sent by the head office, who stated that he was 41 years old, from Guangdong, and was previously the supervisor of students studying in Japan in Nanjing. Two days after the Shanghai branch of Wu Hua Bank went bankrupt, the head office sent a telegram to Nanjing, asking me to represent the liquidation. After I arrived in Shanghai, due to internal disputes, after many twists and turns, I started receiving liquidation. I then sent the branch manager and important staff members to work with the lawyers and accountants hired to manage the accounts. According to the branch managers Fan and Wang, there is a profit of over 100,000 yuan, which is roughly consistent. Now, we are urging the collection of debts, and those who do not pay have been sued. In the future, we plan to first repay the savings deposits and then repay the various current accounts. As for the registration issue, the head office is in Guangzhou. At that time, the revolutionary government had only Guangdong, and the organization was not complete, so we registered with the Finance Department. Later, for the convenience of developing abroad, we also registered with the Hong Kong government. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that there were several points that needed to be investigated. After the branch went bankrupt, two Xiang Sheng cars were hired to move items at the branch. The police checked at the time. Furthermore, the head office allocated 250,000 yuan of capital to the branch, but the plaintiff knew that 220,000 yuan had been withdrawn, which means that the head office had no capital. Also, regarding the registration issue, it was just said that it had been registered with the foreign government of Hong Kong, which should also be certified by the consulate. These three points should be investigated in detail. At this point, after reviewing the previous files and various evidence, the court believed that the evidence was complete, and then ordered the opening of arguments. The eleven lawyers from the plaintiff and defendant each argued, and then the court ordered the conclusion of the arguments and scheduled the sentencing for the 19th. It was already 7 o'clock when the court adjourned.

Private Postal Agencies Still Being Penalized 190

Even with Stamps Affixed and Canceled by the Ningbo Post Office

Because Post Office Cannot Reach All Locations Simultaneously

The Ministry of Communications, because private postal agencies were hindering the development of the postal service, ordered all private postal agencies to cease operations from January 1st of this year and not to collect or deliver letters. However, on the 9th of this month, Lu Youtong, an employee of the Shanghai Postal Administration, discovered Zhang Xiuhe, a messenger from the Baoshun Private Postal Agency at 366 Jiujiang Road, delivering letters in Jiu An Li, Yunnan Road. He reported this to the police and Zhang was detained by the General Police Station. After questioning by the police chief, in addition to submitting 108 letters and checks to the First Special District Court for seizure, the owner of the Baoshun Agency, Dong Fufa from Ningbo, was summoned to be prosecuted. This was reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Chinese detective Gao Yanrong summoned Dong Xiangfa and Zhang Xiuhe to the Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu clarified the case and filed a lawsuit according to Articles 5 and 27 of the Postal Regulations, requesting punishment according to the law. When questioned, Dong Xiangfa confessed that the Baoshun Private Postal Agency was operated by Lin A Si, and I was employed as an accountant. We have now stopped operations in accordance with the order. These letters are from the Ningbo Money Dealers Association. Because the post office often delivers letters at the same location in the morning and afternoon, and cannot reach all locations simultaneously, a temporary solution was agreed upon with the Ningbo Post Office. The letters from the Money Dealers Association were affixed with sufficient postage and sent to the post office to be canceled, and then taken to Shanghai by ship and delivered by me. This was permitted by the post office, so the detained letters were all affixed with postage and stamped by the post office. The Shanghai Flower Trade Association is also currently using this method. When questioned, Zhang Xiuhe confessed that he was employed by Dong to deliver letters and knew nothing else. The presiding judge Zhan Liangce immediately asked Lu Youtong, the representative of the post office, whether the post office in Ningbo had allowed this to happen. The answer was that this would never happen. The court asked why the letters were all stamped by the post office. The answer was that this may be because some small employees who did not understand the reasoning believed that since sufficient postage had been affixed and the postal revenue had not been reduced, it would be fine to deliver the letters themselves, so they stamped them. This was actually an error in procedure. After Judge Zhan verified the confessions, he announced in court that Dong Xiangfa was found guilty of operating a postal business and fined 80 yuan, and Zhang Xiuhe was found guilty of assisting and fined 40 yuan. If they cannot pay the fine, they will be sentenced to imprisonment, with 2 yuan equivalent to one day. The detained letters will be delivered to the addressees by the post office in accordance with the postal regulations.

Jiangbei Workers' Bloody Fight Turns into Murder 191

Guo Xinren Dies from Serious Injuries

Cai Bukui Confesses to Revenge

Regarding the violent fight among dock ruffians near the Yongyu Yarn Factory in Caojiadu, Huxi, by the Suzhou Creek around 10 AM the day before yesterday, which resulted in four seriously injured individuals, one of whom was in critical condition, and the arrest of three suspects including Cai Bukui by the police, as reported in yesterday's newspaper, it is now known that Guo Xinren, 29 years old, from Bao'ying, Jiangbei, died at 11:20 AM yesterday in the Red Cross Hospital due to three knife wounds to the head. The hospital notified the Caojiadu branch bureau, and Director Wang immediately dispatched police to instruct the local officials to report to the local court for inspection. Meanwhile, the other three injured individuals, Xu Zuozhi, Zhang Fucai, and Chen Xuegu, were treated by doctors with bandages and medication before being detained at the bureau. Bureau member Liu interrogated them separately. According to Xu Zuozhi, 30 years old, from Bao'ying, this morning he was buying melon seeds from a woman named Dong Cuiying at the dock and had a slight argument. Unexpectedly, Cai Bukui led dozens of followers, each carrying sharp blades and iron bars, and rushed over, violently beating and slashing them, resulting in a severed right finger and leg injuries from the bars, rendering him unable to move. Xu Maoren, 50 years old, stated that Zuozhi is his son, and his account was similar. Zhang Fucai and Chen Xuegu also stated that they and Guo Xinren, upon seeing Cai and his gang attacking Xu, stepped forward to mediate but were instead attacked with stabs and beatings, resulting in two or three knife wounds each and bar injuries to their backs. Cai Bukui, 37 years old, from Bao'ying, confessed that Xu Zuozhi and his gang had been acting lawlessly at the dock, extorting one yuan from each arriving ship. When he tried to intervene the other day, they gathered a gang and destroyed the furniture in his shop. Therefore, he beat them in retaliation. The woman, Dong Cuiying, provided a similar statement. After obtaining the confessions, the bureau member considered the case to involve loss of life and specially prepared documents to be submitted to the Public Security Bureau for review.

Winter Exhibiting Spring Climate Makes Agricultural Prospects Bleak 193

Since the beginning of winter, the weather in this city has been unusually warm, with the Fahrenheit scale often around 50 degrees, resembling springtime. People feel hot even in thin cotton clothes, leading to a daily increase in throat ailments. According to farmers in the Huxi area yesterday, the recent climate has been harsh and warm. Vegetables in the fields have sprouted swords, broad beans are already bearing fruit, wheat is growing vigorously, and some rapeseed is even blooming. This phenomenon is rare in recent years. Public Utilities Bureau to Implement Bicycle Registration 194

License Fee of 50 Cents, Annual Fee of 3 Yuan

The Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau issued a notice regarding the implementation of bicycle registration: "The Bureau plans to implement bicycle registration. The Municipal Government approved the plan on December 28 with instruction number 12838. It is now determined that the registration will begin on January 21. All registration procedures have been drafted by the Bureau. All bicycle shop owners are hereby notified. Special notice. Director Xu Peihuang." The registration procedures are excerpted as follows: (1) Private bicycles will use green plates with blue characters, and commercial bicycles will use white plates with blue characters. Numbers 1 to 40,000 are designated for private license plates, and 40,001 to 50,000 are for commercial license plates. (2) After registration, all private and commercial bicycles must be stamped with a steel seal for identification. The numbers will remain unchanged during future license renewals or transfers. (3) Private bicycle owners must bring their property tickets with their names and addresses when registering to ensure the accuracy of the information. The registration form can be filled out by Bureau staff. Commercial bicycle registration forms will be issued to the Bicycle Rental Association for completion and returned to the Bureau with the seal of each commercial bicycle shop. (4) Registration locations will be temporarily divided into four areas: (A) The Bureau's Main Vehicle Office at Fenglin Bridge will handle the registration of commercial vehicles in all districts, as well as private vehicles in the French Concession and the southern and western parts of the Shanghai International Settlement. (B) The Zhabei Vehicle Office will handle the registration of private vehicles in northern Shanghai. (C) The Wusong Vehicle Office will handle the registration of private vehicles in Wusong. (D) The Pudong Yangtang Vehicle Office will handle the registration of private vehicles in Pudong. (5) Registration dates are from January 21 to February 15. (6) Bicycles will be arranged in order of arrival on the Bureau's specially made wooden frames for numbering. A round cardboard token will be issued to each bicycle owner, which they can use to register at the designated window. After registration, they can use the vehicle license to obtain the vehicle with the steel seal. (7) During this bicycle registration period, in addition to the registration procedures being free of charge, each vehicle must pay a license fee of 50 cents and an annual fee of 3 yuan.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Issues Notice to Postpone Bicycle Inspections 195

The Municipal Public Security Bureau issued a notice to all its branch bureaus yesterday: "In accordance with the Public Utilities Bureau's letter, the Bureau has set the period from January 21 to February 15 for conducting bicycle registration in the city. All bicycle license renewals this year should be extended to begin on January 21. Old bicycles that have not been registered or renewed are allowed to temporarily operate with their old licenses. New vehicles will be issued temporary permits by the Bureau for temporary use, all valid until February 15. In addition to notifying the Finance Bureau separately, this is hereby notified to all branch bureaus for their information and to instruct their subordinates accordingly."

All Sectors of the City Commemorated Pan Hongsheng Yesterday 197

More than 1,000 Representatives from Various Groups Attended

Wu Zhihao Presided Over the Memorial Service; the Atmosphere Was Particularly Solemn and Tragic

Xin Xin She reports: "The memorial service for the patriotic martyr Pan Hongsheng, organized by all sectors of Shanghai, was held at 2 PM yesterday at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce auditorium in Tianhou Palace Bridge. More than 1,000 representatives from various groups, including Wang Xiaolai, Wu Zhihao, and Shen Tianxin, attended. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau and the police authorities of the concessions also dispatched personnel to maintain order. The atmosphere was peaceful and orderly. Details are as follows."

Venue Arrangement 198

The venue was set up in the auditorium of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. A plain floral archway was erected in front of the door, with a white cloth banner hanging above, reading "Shanghai Representatives of All Circles Memorial Service for Pan Hongsheng, Martyr." On the stage in the auditorium, a portrait of Sun Yat-sen and the national flag were hung in the center, with a portrait of Pan Hongsheng

(Photographed by Qichang) 199

Martyr below. A plain-colored warm pavilion was also built on the stage in the center. On both sides hung elegiac couplets from Ju Zheng, President of the Judicial Yuan. To the right of the stage was the alarm bell of the China Police Bell Association. Below the stage was the press seat. The upstairs was the seat of the orphanage military band. White cloth elegiac couplets were hung all around. The layout was solemn and tragic.

Attending Representatives 200

Yesterday, the presidium included Wang Xiaolai, Chen Jicheng, Zhu Xuefan, Yu Zhenhui, Hu Fengxiang, Qu Zhenhua, Shen Tianxin, the officiant Wu Zhihao, the attendants Tao Leqin, Liu Zhongying, Zhang Xianfang, and Chen Jiufeng, Chen Binghui, Zhu Zhichun, Wang Jingdong, Yu Yaoqiu, Li Manyun, Cai Qiaojun, as well as representatives from various groups, schools, and shops, totaling more than 1,000 people.

Memorial Ceremony 201

At precisely 1 PM, the Police Bell Association began to ring the bell. The entire venue was silent, only the sound of the bell could be heard, which was quite alerting. At 2 PM, the participants arrived one after another, and the ceremony began. First, the orphanage military band played mourning music, and then they paid the highest respect to the national flag, the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, and the portrait of Pan Hongsheng. After the salute, they observed three minutes of silence to mourn. After the silence, Wu Zhihao offered incense, laid a wreath, and read the memorial text.

Report on Deeds 202

After the ceremony, Chen Jicheng reported on his deeds, saying, "Today is the memorial service for Martyr Pan Hongsheng. Representatives from all walks of life have come to attend the memorial service because they deeply regret the martyr's passing. This shows the general sympathy. Regarding the martyr's deeds during his lifetime, there are many things that are worth commemorating. Now, I will give a brief report below. Martyr Pan was born in Wuxi County, Jiangsu Province. He was upright by nature. In the 14th year of the Republic, when he was 13 years old, he was studying in Qingdao. It happened to be the time when the May 30th Incident occurred in Shanghai. He knew that we must unite sincerely in order to resist foreign insults, so he invited his classmates to raise donations and appeal everywhere. It can be seen that he had a deep sense of national consciousness when he was alive. He came to Shanghai the following year and studied at Fufeng Paper Company. Soon after, the September 18th Incident occurred. After hearing the news, he was so angry that he wanted to die, so he joined the Shanghai Civilian Volunteer Army for training. The following year, the Japanese invaders invaded Shanghai. He was ordered to assist the 19th Route Army in fighting in Baoshan. After the ceasefire agreement, in June, he graduated from the 19th Route Army training and returned to his old job. Unexpectedly, at that time, dishonest merchants in the city were competing to sell enemy goods, disregarding shame. He held a bullet warning and was arrested and sentenced to six years in prison. Unexpectedly, he died last year due to excessive injuries." After the speech, Wu Zhihao, Shen Tianxin, and others delivered speeches one after another. The meeting adjourned at 4 PM.

Relatives of Victims of the Tongfu Wheel Surrounded Lawyer Zhang Henghai Yesterday 203

Demanding Additional Compensation

They Were Dispersed After Police Suppression

Dagong She reports: "A Tongfu Wheel of the Tongan Shipping Company sank off the coast of Mokpo, Korea, in October last year after being hit by a hurricane. No crew members survived. Bao Anfu, the manager of the company in Shanghai, rushed to Japan immediately after receiving the news and entrusted the Japan Maritime Rescue Society to try to salvage the ship. However, the ship could not be found. After two weeks, more than 10,000 gold coins were spent. Because the seabed off the coast of Mokpo is extremely deep, it is not easy to search for once it sinks. After this news reached Shanghai, the families of the Tongfu Wheel crew members were all in Shanghai. They immediately organized a group and negotiated with lawyer Zhang Henghai, the agent of Bao Anfu. At that time, because the insurance money for the wheel had not yet been received, Bao Anfu lacked funds for compensation, so the negotiations were fruitless. Recently, Bao Anfu received the insurance money in Japan and remitted more than 7,000 yuan, and also wrote to lawyer Zhang Henghai to represent him in distributing compensation to the crew members. Lawyer Zhang immediately published a notice in the newspaper to inform the families of the victims to go and collect the money. This advertisement was published yesterday. Unexpectedly, at about 8 AM yesterday, the families of the victims, supporting the old and carrying the young, went to lawyer Zhang's office at No. 692 Niuzhuang Road. Unexpectedly, more than 100 people gathered. The amount of compensation set by Bao Anfu was a maximum of 750 yuan and a minimum of 180 yuan, which they said was not satisfactory. Lawyer Zhang replied that this amount was calculated based on ten times the monthly salary of each person. If they wanted to increase it, he had no right to agree. He had to telegraph Bao Anfu to get his consent before he could do so. However, the families demanded that the increase be issued immediately. So they surrounded Lawyer Zhang in the office. At that time, there were many people talking and the order was chaotic. They confronted each other until about 3 PM. Lawyer Zhang happened to have just recovered from a new illness and had not eaten all day. He was in a terrible state. He had no choice but to send a clerk to report to the Old Gate Patrol Room. The patrol head dispatched a detective to stop them, telling them that obstructing freedom violated criminal law. At that time, the families of the victims, seeing the detective arriving, began to leave one after another. The detective thought that the families of the victims were extremely pitiful, so he did not arrest them. It was not until about 4 PM that the detective protected Lawyer Zhang and sent him home for dinner, while the elderly, weak, women, and children were still guarding the office. It was not until the lights of thousands of homes were lit that they had not yet dispersed."

The Case of Lin Yujin Suing Sheng Yuchang for Abandonment Was Heard Once Yesterday 204

Research on Repeated Cohabitation

The Defendant Flatly Denies

Sheng Yuchang, 38 years old, the eldest grandson of Sheng Xingsun, the former Minister of Posts and Communications of the Qing Dynasty and a native of Changzhou, lives at No. 1 Beidang Road, French Concession. He was recently sued by Lin Yujin, a Guangdong woman living upstairs at the Jinhua Pharmacy at No. 291 Xiafei Road, for abandonment, with an attached civil lawsuit to recover 50,000 yuan in maintenance fees. After receiving the complaint, the court had summoned the defendant twice through Judge Xiong Huiping. The defendant also hired a lawyer to defend him. Because the witnesses had not arrived, the court ordered to postpone the hearing to summon the witnesses again, and ordered the plaintiff Lin Yujin to submit to a medical examination at the forensic office to check the condition of her lung disease for verification. The plaintiff's lawsuit and the defendant's defense intentions have been described in detail in previous reports. Yesterday, the case was summoned for continued hearing. He requested a chair to make a statement. The court approved it and announced a new trial. According to the plaintiff Lin Yujin's statement, when I was sixteen years old, I was originally a prostitute in a brothel. After being introduced by a Mr. Su, I met the defendant and married him as a concubine in the first month of that year. We lived together for more than two years. Because the defendant had many concubines, I could not stand the squeeze. I left and had no way to make a living. I spent my days dancing in dance halls. In the year the Japanese fought, I met the defendant in the dance hall in October. He came with his concubine. Because I was sick, I asked the defendant to help me out of compassion. The defendant ordered his concubine to give me 200 yuan. He came again the next night. He told me that he could restore my previous status. Later, I rented a house with him at No. 291 Xiafei Road. He gave me expenses ranging from 200 to 300 yuan per month until March of this year (referring to the lunar calendar), when he suddenly disappeared and stopped paying the daily expenses. I am now seriously ill. He cruelly abandoned me and had no choice but to sue him. The defendant Sheng Yuchang admitted that he married the plaintiff as a concubine in the 11th year of the Republic and lived together for more than a year. In the year the Fengzhi War occurred (i.e., the 13th year), she voluntarily left. I tried to persuade her to stay, but she refused, so I let her go freely. I have not seen her since. There was no such thing as meeting in the dance hall, giving 200 yuan, or renting a house together. The officer asked the defendant if she was suing you because she was sick and pitiful. Can you give her some money to settle the matter? Sheng replied that he could not admit it. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that the landlord Chen Zhang and neighbor Cao Fusheng were in court today and requested to call them as witnesses. The court immediately called Chen Zhang to the stand. According to her statement, Lin Yujin is my tenant. She lives with a servant. I went to her room two or three times to collect rent. I saw the defendant sitting in the room. Cao Fusheng stated that I have lived upstairs in this house for four or five years. Lin Yujin lives in the front building. I have seen the defendant's face about ten times. When they rented the house together, I saw it. Once, when the defendant came, because the maid lived on the third floor, I went to open the door and let the defendant in. The officer asked the defendant again if he knew the two witnesses. He replied that he did not know them and had never seen them before. At this point, the officer ordered the debate to begin. After the lawyers of both parties debated with each other, the court ordered the debate to be suspended because the case still needed to be investigated and ordered to wait for a scheduled re-hearing.

Retrial of Wang Xinggao in the Case of the Assassination of Tang Jiapeng Postponed 209

Reply from Wuchang Has Not Arrived

The Officer Ordered a Stop to Visitation

Tang Jiapeng, a Ningbo native and former manager of the Great World Amusement Park, was shot and killed in front of the Great World at about 1 AM on the morning of June 18 of the year before last. At the same time, a pedestrian, Wu Guangcai from Yangzhou, was killed by stray bullets. After the incident, the French Patrol House apprehended two suspects, Zhang Tinggui and Zhao Guangfu, confiscated a handgun, and sent them to the court. Zhang was sentenced to 20 years in prison, and Zhao was sentenced to life imprisonment, with each being deprived of their civil rights. Zhang's sentence has been finalized and he has been sent to prison. Zhao is still appealing to the Supreme Court. Recently, Chinese and Western detectives from the French Patrol House arrested Wang Xinggao (39 years old, a native of Funing, living at No. 46 Menggu Road, Zhabei), a key suspect in the case, in Room 537 of the Central Hotel on Guangdong Road on the evening of December 13 of last year. He was brought together with the already captured Zhang and Zhao for questioning. After the investigation was completed, he was transferred to the Second Special District Court, and a public prosecution was filed against him for premeditated murder. Judge Xiong Huiping opened a court for interrogation on December 26 of the same month. Because Wang denied participating in the instigation of the murder and stated that he was a warden in the First Prison in Wuchang, Hubei that year, he was ordered to be detained pending the transfer of documents to the Wuchang Court in Hubei for investigation. After the reply arrives, the hearing will be held again. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday was the date for the continued hearing. Judge Xiong presided over the first criminal court. Lawyer Gu Shouxi appeared in court on behalf of the Police Department, and the defendant's defense lawyer also appeared in court to await instructions. The officer briefly questioned the defendant and then announced that the investigative reply from the Wuchang Court had not yet been received and could not be heard. The hearing was rescheduled for the 23rd. The defendant was still returned to the detention center and visitation was stopped.

Private Use of Account Funds, Knife Cuts to Genitals and Testicles 210

Shao Hongmao's Pursuit of Women Results in Tragedy

Shao Hongmao, an 18-year-old from Ningbo, living at No. 38 Shouxing Lane, Fangbang Bridge, works as a salesman at the Lihua Gasoline Refinery in this city. Although Shao's monthly income is limited, he often pursues women and spends extravagantly, making it difficult to maintain economic stability. He often felt panic. Soon after, he privately misappropriated account funds from the factory he was handling. The matter was discovered by the manager, who severely reprimanded him and ordered him to return the funds immediately. Seeing that the matter had been exposed and fearing that it would affect his job, Shao tried desperately to raise the money, but to no avail. Looking back on the past, he suddenly felt resentment. In a moment of impulse, at about 6 PM yesterday, he used a knife to cut off his genitals and testicles in the factory building. He immediately fell to the ground in extreme pain, rolling and wailing. The matter was heard by colleagues, who went in to see what was happening and saw Shao's lower body covered in blood. Knowing that there was an accident, they quickly reported it to the patrol room, which sent an ambulance to fly him to Renji Hospital for treatment. The doctor examined him and gave him emergency treatment, but the injury was too severe and his condition was very critical.

Two Robbers Each Sentenced to Eight Years 211

Hu ChunChao and Li Fugui Commit Multiple Crimes

On the morning of the 29th of last month, at 8:30, robbers Hu ChunChao and Li Fugui, each holding a wooden fake pistol, went to rob the property of a local woman, Yu Xu, at No. 74 Taoyuan Lane, Beikaier Road. The woman tightly closed the door and shouted for help from the window. Hu and others panicked, broke open the door, abandoned their guns, and fled. Chinese detective Huang Fugen, and Chinese policemen No. 636 and No. 297 intercepted them, and brought them and the fake guns to Huishan Patrol Room, and sent them to the First Special District Court. The investigation revealed that between October and December of last year, they colluded with a gang to rob Hu Hengxiang at No. 245 Tongli, Gu Guishi at No. 1027 DongbailaoHui Road, and Zhang Shishi at No. 56 Huishan Road, robbing them of more than 150 yuan worth of property. Yesterday morning, the patrol room sent the two defendants back to the Third Criminal Court. 工部局 lawyer Li Zhishan gave a detailed account of the previous situation, and presented the fake gun as evidence, requesting a strict investigation. The judge then examined the confession of the two defendants. Judge Xiao Xie Fen sentenced Hu ChunChao and Li Fugui to eight years of imprisonment each. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized will be counted as two days offsetting one day of imprisonment, and the fake gun will be confiscated.

Three Thieves Break into a Home on Carter Road 212

A Housewife's Gold Bracelet

Snatched, They Fled with Shouts

At approximately 11:40 AM yesterday, at the residence of a certain Mr. [Surname] at No. 31, Lane 146, Carter Road, while the family was preparing a meal, three robbers suddenly appeared. Each was armed with a handgun. One robber stood guard outside while the other two entered the house. They first held the people inside at bay, forbidding them to make any noise. Then, they demanded the occupants hand over valuables. As the head of the household could not comply immediately, the robbers noticed a gold bracelet on the housewife's wrist. They forcibly seized it, then ransacked the inner rooms, overturning chests and boxes, and searching everything. As a result, they also made off with thirty-six dollars in paper money before fleeing with shouts. Afterward, the homeowner reported the incident to the local police station, requesting an investigation and arrest.

"One Arrow, Two Eagles" Accused of Rape and Detained 213

Bu Fazong Denies Committing Rape

Two Women Identify Him in Court

Cheng Lanying, a sixteen-year-old woman from Taizhou, residing at No. 4037 Yangzhou Road, and Qiao Xiuying, a fifteen-year-old woman, also from Taizhou, residing at No. 1128 Weituoma Road, both work as female laborers at the Hengfeng Cotton Mill on Huasheng Road. They possess slight beauty and a frivolous demeanor. Recently, they became romantically involved with Bu Fazong, a 22-year-old male laborer from Qingjiang working at the Yihe Cotton Mill on Taopeng Road. On the night before last, around 9:00 PM, Bu seized an opportunity to lure the two women to the Liaoyang Hotel at No. 106 Liaoyang Road, where he booked room number 14, achieving "one arrow, two eagles." The next morning, each returned home. After being questioned thoroughly by their parents, Cheng Zhaozhang and Qiao Chuqing, the situation was revealed. They reported it to the Yulin Road Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Detective Sun Zhenqing and Chinese Constable No. 58 to secretly apprehend Bu Fazong and detain him at the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District. A lawyer from the Public Works Department, Li Zhishan, presented the case. Subsequently, Cheng Zhaozhang and Qiao Chuqing testified to the events. The defendant claimed that there were a total of four men in the room that night, including himself, and that he had no improper relations with either of the women. However, the women, Lanying and Xiuying, identified the defendant as the one who had indeed raped them. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered him to remain in custody, postponing the case for further investigation. The two women, Cheng and Qiao, were sent to the forensic medical office for examination.

Shaoxing Wine Trade Association Holds Meeting Yesterday 214

The Shanghai Shaoxing Wine Trade Association held its 13th joint executive and supervisory committee meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM. Committee members Song Jinrong, Zhou Jinrong, Zhou Zhaojun, Lu Songgao, Tang Hanmin, and Fang Changsheng attended, with Zhou Jinrong serving as chairman. The following resolutions were passed: (1) The association has created four types of tables, including economic revenue and expenditure monthly reports, as well as various receipts and forms. The question of whether these are appropriate was put to a vote. (4) A report was made on the association's property tax. The Land Bureau and Finance Bureau have jointly approved, and the city government has now approved, that the association's property be exempt from land value tax as a public utility for municipal groups. (5) Members Shen Dazhou and Ji Sheng reported that Suzhous Derun Shen had engaged in breach of contract, and the question of how to proceed was put to a vote. It was resolved that a letter should be sent to the Suzhou Association, informing Derun Shen and awaiting a response before further action. All five items were unanimously approved, and the meeting was adjourned.

Inspection Report of the China Land Reclamation Bank 219

The China Land Reclamation Bank's report on the inspection of its issuance reserves states that the bank's issuance and business treasuries have always been completely separate. According to the bank's regulations, the cash reserve should be above 70%, and the guarantee reserve should be below 30%. On the 12th of this month, accountant Wang Zikang, along with representatives of the board of directors and supervisors Xu Jikui and Xu Busun, conducted an inspection. The results are as follows: The total amount of exchange certificate reserves is 7,095,000 silver dollars, of which the cash reserve is 5,268,000 silver dollars, and the guarantee reserve is 1,827,000 silver dollars. The cash reserve is above 70%, and the guarantee reserve is below 30%. This report is issued on the 12th of January, 1935.

Looking up at the fragrant traces of Yi Xian, one can vaguely obtain it. Compared to the gorgeousness of Zhao Dong, there is an abundance of strange energy. He is truly a treasure of China and a heavenly being of this world. Currently, he is briefly resting on the coast. If there are those who wish to see his true work, why not visit him? The mailing address is the Cihang Pictorial Society, No. 27 Renji Lane, Ximen Road, French Concession.

Zhejiang Education Department Petitions Provincial Government to Quickly Allocate One Million Yuan in Local Bonds to Alleviate Immediate Needs 229

Schools in Various Counties Unable to Maintain Operations and Gradually Closing

Teachers Suffering Greatly, No Different from Disaster Victims

Xu Shaodi, the Director of the Education Department of Zhejiang Province, stated that the province suffered a severe drought last year, causing education in various counties to come to a standstill. He has specially petitioned the provincial government to promptly instruct the Finance Department to allocate one million yuan in local bonds, designated as educational reserve funds. The original petition stated: "The various counties in this province have suffered a severe drought, with crops damaged. The disaster area is almost the entire province. We have successively received official letters from the Provincial Party Headquarters, as well as joint petitions from county governments, local groups, and educational institutions, and reports from the heads of various education bureaus to the province. Education is unable to save itself, and they are all requesting the allocation of provincial funds for relief. It has been found that the educational funds of various counties have been exhausted due to the disaster, causing education to come to a standstill. The previous director requested the allocation of one million yuan in local bonds from this province to serve as educational reserve funds for relief, and requested that the original regulations for the reserve fund be revised to facilitate implementation. This was approved at the 732nd meeting of the Provincial Government Committee, and the regulations were revised and submitted to the Legal Review Committee to organize the clauses. Subsequently, the regulations were reviewed and approved at the 734th meeting of the Government Committee. Now, it has been found that the educational funds of various counties are becoming increasingly tight, and the accumulated arrears are increasing. The counties with the most arrears have reached eight or nine months, and the least have three months. The average arrears have been more than five months. Schools are unable to maintain operations and are gradually closing. The counties with the most closures, such as Jiangshan, have reached 86 schools, accounting for 40% of the county's schools. Dongyang has 85 schools, accounting for 30% of the county's schools. The remaining counties have closures of 50 to 60 schools, 30 to 40 schools, and more than 10 schools, varying in number. The material and spiritual suffering of teachers in various counties is no different from that of disaster victims. If relief is not provided quickly, it will lead to starvation. Various counties have complied with orders to tighten their budgets, which have been reduced again and again, but revenue has not been secured. Demands for salaries and strikes are inevitable. The county government is unable to cope and is in a desperate situation. These are all facts. Therefore, in recent days, this government and various responsible departments have successively received requests from various counties to allocate funds as soon as possible to alleviate immediate needs. This is no different from waiting for aid. Moreover, it is the time for commercial settlement, and it is especially important to complete the settlement before the deadline to avoid being too late. Education is one of the psychological constructions. Maintaining the nearly extinct musical strings is as important and urgent as providing disaster relief. Therefore, we have attached the table of the post-disaster situation of education funds in various counties and respectfully request that you examine and instruct the Finance Department to quickly transfer the one million yuan in local bonds designated as educational reserve funds to this department for distribution in accordance with the regulations. At the same time, please submit it to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for review and approval."

Ministry of Finance Replies That Salt Tax in Henan Province Cannot Be Allocated for Educational Expenses 230

The Ministry of Finance recently replied to the Ministry of Education, stating that it has received a consultation from the Henan Teachers Association requesting the allocation of salt tax to subsidize educational expenses. After checking, the continued collection of sales tax in Henan Province is for the application of the Huai Lu production area, and it is difficult for Henan Province to allocate it. Moreover, the Henan Lu surtax has been reduced. The various sections mentioned in the original petition of the association were based on a misunderstanding. A special consultation is made for your information and transfer.

Chronicle of Tongde Medical College's New Campus 249

Wu Zhihui

Tongde Medical College's new campus is completed. I will carve a brief history of the college on stone to inform future generations. President Gu Yuqi asked me to write an article. According to the historical records, this college was founded in the seventh year of the Republic of China. Mr. Shen Tanfei proposed it, and the German Medical Association expressed its sympathy and support. It was then established and named the Private Shanghai Tongde Medical College. Mr. Jiang Fengzhi was appointed as the principal, and the school building was rented on Machen Road. The funds were raised, and the equipment was very simple. Scholars came in droves. In the spring of the eighth year, a practicing hospital was attached to Qingdao Road. The inspectors of the Ministry of Education praised it for being able to meet the urgent needs. Donations from all parties gradually increased, and the chemistry practice room and other rooms were gradually completed. More and more scholars came, and famous people from Shanghai were invited to organize the Board of Directors. The foundation of the school was thus solidified. In the autumn of the ninth year, the Board of Directors and the Committee jointly decided to make it coeducational. The number of female students suddenly reached more than ten. By the eleventh year, the total number of students in the school had reached more than one hundred. The school building was repeatedly rented and expanded, and research rooms for bacteria and pathology, and an anatomy room were added. Adult corpses were formally dissected so that students could practically understand the internal organization of the human body. At that time, it was flourishing. In July of the thirteenth year, it was suddenly interrupted due to a small matter. Mr. Huang Zhong was replaced as the principal, Mr. Zheng Bangyan as the hospital director, and Mr. Pang Jingzhou as the director of affairs. They worked together with one heart and endured hardships to maintain the situation. In the fourteenth year, Mr. Huang resigned from the position of principal, and Mr. Pang succeeded him. Because the Board of Directors and the Committee could not be gathered temporarily, Mr. Pang alone shouldered the responsibility of the school and devoted himself to improvement. But the economy was exhausted. Fortunately, Mr. Huang Chuqiu gave generously, and Mr. Pang again paid a large sum of money, so the school was able to stabilize. In the fifteenth year, the articles of association of the Board of Directors were revised, and seven directors were elected to be responsible for supervision and command, and filed with the Ministry of Education. School affairs were becoming more and more prosperous, and students from all over the world, from Korea in the north to Yunnan and Guangdong in the south, praised it as a famous school. Gu, because there were not many classrooms and the wards were narrow, development was hindered. Mr. Pang changed the rented school building to Tongfu Road, and asked acquaintances to borrow tens of thousands of taels of construction fees. With the consent of the owner of the house in the adjacent open space, classrooms and wards were added. It was completed in June of the sixteenth year. In the same year, the Tongde School Journal was also launched. In the seventeenth year, the Minister of Health of the League of Nations, Mr. Lachmann, and the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, Mr. Hu Hongji, visited the school and expressed their deep appreciation. In the twenty-first year, Mr. Pang also resigned from the position of principal due to other matters. At that time, the Shanghai war was in full swing, and the Board of Directors could not be gathered. Therefore, Mr. Gu Yuqi, Mr. Zeng Liqun, etc., organized a committee and appointed Mr. Gu as the chairman to maintain school affairs. The directors were then summoned and resolved to formally appoint Mr. Gu as the president and hospital director. He worked hard and school affairs were progressing day by day. In September of that year, the Board of Directors was approved by the Ministry of Education. It was then seen that the Tongfu Road school building was still insufficient for development. In the winter of the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, a general meeting of all directors was held, and Mr. Shao Lizi was elected as the chairman of the Board of Directors, and Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Pang Jingzhou, and Gu Yuqi were elected as executive directors. Mr. Gu was appointed as the president. The Board of Directors decided to organize a new school building construction committee. Many donors from all parties were willing to help. Mr. Pan Gongzhan served as the executive director and member of the construction committee, and he worked hard with President Gu to plan and organize. Through the introduction of Mr. Cheng Mutun, he was able to purchase the houses and land of the former Health Experiment Institute's smallpox department on Xiangyin Road in the city center, covering an area of more than five acres and eight points. There were twelve large buildings and five large bungalows, but it was still not enough to be deployed. It was decided to add a large auditorium, six classrooms, and thirty-two dormitories. The sanitary and other facilities in each dormitory were well-equipped. Construction began in January of the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China and was completed in three months. This became the beginning of Tongde College having its own school building. All things develop, if you get the right people, you can gradually accumulate into a geometric proportion. Tongde's achievements in fifteen years have been like this. If you add another fifteen years, its grand situation will be ten or a hundred times greater than today, which is certain. Then, the beauty of the building without the best can be guaranteed by this stone. January of the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China, Wu Jingheng of Wujin wrote this.

The A Team Wins the Inter-Port Trial Match in Bitter Wind and Rain 253

The B Team's Lineup Was Disorganized, Losing 3-8

The A Team's Talented Players Put on a Wonderful Performance

Jinshun, Colasa, and Baoshali Are the Heroes

The Shanghai Inter-Port Football Team Trial Match was held at Yiyuan at 3:00 PM yesterday. The wind and rain were bitter, and the scene was bleak. There were only three or four thousand spectators. Both teams arrived on time, unlike the perfunctory approach of previous years. However, the field was muddy, making it difficult to run. Although the situation was not very tense, all the players showed their skills, and the performance was wonderful and very satisfactory. In the first half, the situation was even, and the A team led by 2-1. In the second half, the inside forwards of the B team could not coordinate, while the forwards of the A team, such as Baoshali, Colasa, and Sun Jinshun, added to the glory, like tigers with wings. The connection was wonderful, and they made repeated achievements, and the shots were cleverly placed, leaving Shi Meisi at a loss. It was truly a sight to behold. As a result, the A team won a big victory by 8-3. The lineups of the two teams are as follows:

The Situation in the First Half, Mutual Respect 254

The lineups of the two teams had already been announced, but Dai Linjing was absent due to injury, and Cash intentionally retired and did not want to participate. It had been predetermined that Feng Yunyou and Colasa would replace them. Zhong Yongshen was temporarily absent due to some reason, and the old man Lux Hart Bacon appeared. Both sides kicked off in the rain and wind, and the situation was quite even. Both sides had opportunities to attack, but they did not succeed. Moreover, because it was a trial match, there was mutual respect and no anger. Therefore, the performance was more clear and beautiful, and the fans were paying attention to each player's performance. The victory or defeat was put behind them. If the official game could be like this, then there would be no unexpected disputes in the football world.

Lao Sun Scores Repeatedly 255

The A team's forwards were very sharp. The B team became a multi-event autumn because the strength of the middle forward line was slightly weak. Sun Jinshun, Colasa, and Baoshali echoed each other, just right, very wonderful. At ten minutes, Sun Jinshun opened the scoring, thanks to the help of Ke Bao. He scored in the left inside forward position. The B team once pursued, and Yichen and Jiaqiu both had shots on goal, but they were either saved or missed. Lao Sun raised his iron feet and shot into the goal. Smithon dived in and the A team won 2-0.

Returning a Goal 256

After that, Lao Sun had another chance to shoot, but he missed. The B team worked hard, and Colett was very brave. Chen Jiaqiu was well-adjusted, and Hart Bacon sent a high ball. Hewat missed a header, and Colett also headed the ball to attack, but the ball hit the crossbar and fell under the goal, and was caught by Cockran. Li Yichen went deep again, and Lemidi could not catch up. The two chased to the goal, and the goalkeeper rushed out to save the ball. Unexpectedly, A'erjie rushed up and flicked the ball into the goal, and the inside team pulled back a city. Before the center could kick off, the first half was over.

Situation in the Second Half, the A Team Wins Repeatedly 257

In the second half, the performance of the A team was even more wonderful and can be called a spectacle. Therefore, I have to wet my pen and stretch out the paper to describe it in detail to give to the readers. After the kick-off, Chen Jiaqiu made a long shot that was quickly saved. The forwards of the A team fought each other and showed their brilliance. Colasa and Baoshali rushed in and Sun Jinshun followed up. He used a high ball to pick over the defense line. Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Children's Year 271

— Yan Xinquan

What Should Children Be Like?

Little friends! This year has been designated as "Children's Year," and I think you already know that! So, what should children themselves be like during Children's Year? I'll mention the most important things:

(1) Exercise your bodies,

(2) Study diligently,

(3) Buy domestic goods,

(4) Practice the New Life Movement.

I hope that every little friend can achieve the four points listed above. If you can, then not only will your personal future be hopeful, but the future of the country will also be hopeful!

Zhu Wengong's Childhood 272

— Dazhai

Zhu Zi, named Xi, posthumously honored as Wengong, was a person of the Song Dynasty. When Wengong was five years old, he read the Classic of Filial Piety and wrote on the book, "Not to be a human if not like this." Because his father was very knowledgeable, he followed his father to study. At the age of fourteen, his father passed away, and he began to study with a teacher according to his father's will. At the age of eighteen, he passed the Jinshi examination. Wengong was interested in learning but had no intention of seeking fame. After completing his term, he resigned from his official position and returned home to study under the renowned teacher Li Tong. Later, he lectured at the Bailudong Academy, established rules for learning, and compiled a complete collection of Neo-Confucianism. Teachers and scholars alike have considered it to be of great value. In addition to lecturing, Wengong also focused on writing. He authored many books, most of which promoted the morality of Confucius and Mencius, such as the Collected Commentaries on the Four Books. Later scholars regarded him as the orthodox interpreter of the classics. His recorded conversations are written in a style similar to modern vernacular Chinese, making them easy to understand. He also wrote Chu Ci Bian Zheng, showing that he did not neglect literary composition. Now, in the main hall of the Confucian Temple, there are twelve tablets of sages, and one of them is him. Although he was a person of the Song Dynasty, far removed from Confucius, his learning was no less than that of Confucius's disciples, so he was specially added to show respect.

Little friends, you should know that the reason why schools have abolished the reading of classics is that classical texts are not easy for young students to understand. However, classical texts have their own value and are not as harmful as floods or ferocious beasts. This is something that must be understood. Vernacular Chinese is valued for its accessibility, but classical Chinese also has its own uses and cannot be completely dismissed. If you read textbooks and say that classical texts have no value, or if you understand some vernacular Chinese and say that classical Chinese has no use, then you are mistaken. Consider that Zhu Wengong aspired to live according to the classics from a young age, and so he ultimately became the orthodox interpreter of the classics, compiled a complete collection of Neo-Confucianism, and was worshiped by later generations. Seeing the great from the small, the success of one's aspirations is truly admirable. Although he advocated the vernacular style, he was also skilled in classical Chinese. If someone had said that classical Chinese was of no use, would he have opposed it in Wengong's time? Would he have still been willing to study it? I am not advocating for the reading of classics, nor am I fond of classical Chinese, but I am telling little friends not to misunderstand, and to learn from Wengong by aspiring to live a life of purpose.

Iron 273

— Zhen

Little friends, please think about it, what is one thing in our daily lives that we cannot do without?

Clothing: Clothes are made by machines, so what are the machines made of?

Food: Whether it's plants or animals, plant chlorophyll or animal hemoglobin, they all contain iron.

Housing: What are the steel frames and all the nails and other accessories in our houses made of?

Transportation: Do cars and ships all have iron in them? Iron is so important, how can we not pay attention to it?

Little friends, you think that iron is a black metal. On the contrary, iron is actually white. So what is black? Black is iron rust.

Iron is a white, hard, lustrous, and malleable metal. It rusts easily in moist air, especially in the carbon dioxide exhaled by people.

Iron can be divided into three types: pig iron, wrought iron, and steel:

1. Pig iron: is hard and brittle, so it cannot be hammered into shape and has no malleability or ductility. What is malleability and ductility? Malleability: For example, a piece of pig iron cannot be hammered into a thin sheet. Ductility: For example, a piece of pig iron cannot be drawn into a thread. Therefore, to make utensils from pig iron, you must first make a mold and pour the pig iron into the mold to form a utensil.

2. Wrought iron: is not hard and not brittle, and has malleability and ductility. It can be hammered into shape. Have you ever seen a blacksmith make a knife? He heats a piece of iron red-hot, and then he hammers it, and before long, it becomes a knife. Wrought iron is easier to make utensils from than pig iron.

3. Steel: is very strong and tough. If it contains too many impurities, it can also be brittle and hard. Steel has even greater uses. What about trains? What about ships? What about springs? What doesn't use steel? And steel has a lot of elasticity.

Unfortunately, China has very few iron-smelting factories, so we rely on foreign iron. Little friends! Work hard! In the future, let's open the world's largest iron-smelting plant! Then you can be considered a useful person.
