Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

New Year Special Issue (3)

Chinese Woodblock Prints of the Past Year 333

— Feng Ye

In this turbulent society, those nude beauty paintings and the like can no longer give us any comfort. What we demand is a new art with strong stimulation. Chinese woodblock art has developed rapidly under this condition. Now I will describe the development in the past year in detail below - because of the lack of reference materials, or some places are not described very well. 1. Research Associations. In Shanghai, we must first mention the MK Woodcut Research Association. The association was established on New Year's Day in 1933. There were more than a dozen members, all of whom were very active young people in the woodcut art movement. They produced a lot of results after only one year of effort. Although their achievements - the content of the works is not very satisfactory, they have indeed gained a lot in terms of skills. Unfortunately, the association did not develop well later. Not long after, the Weiming Woodcut Research Society followed MK. Initially, there were only four members, but later it developed to more than a dozen. In this way, a total of five woodcut collections were published by the end of the year. The output of its works is very amazing, but in terms of quality, it is not as good as MK. However, in any case, the enthusiasm of young people engaged in the woodcut art movement is increasing day by day. In Guangzhou, there is the Modern Woodcut Research Society. The society was organized in the spring of last year. There are more than a dozen members. It has held two or three exhibitions and published a woodcut collection in less than a year, which has won good reviews from the public. In Peiping, there was also an organization of research associations the year before last. I think they are still continuing their efforts now.

2. Exhibitions. As far as I know, there was only one exhibition in Shanghai - the third exhibition of the MK Woodcut Research Association. Guangzhou has had three exhibitions. The third MK wood exhibition had about one hundred works. In terms of skills, it is more advanced than any previous wood exhibition. For example, the skills of Chen Kebai, Yefu, Chen Baozhen, Luo Qingzhen, Chen Fuzhi and others have been quite mature. Unfortunately, there is no new development in the expression methods and the choice of themes. In particular, they have not grasped the core of the era well. For example, the fact that imperialism is attacking us fiercely has not attracted the attention of our writers, because it is almost impossible to find a work with anti-imperialist sentiment in the entire work, which has to be said to be a great regret. I have not seen the wood exhibition of the Modern Woodcut Research Society. Although some people say that it has received good reviews from the society, I don't think it will be more advanced than that of Shanghai. It can be clearly seen from Li Hua's "Rest of the Hoeing Workers", "Harvest" and "Abandoned Woman", "Egyptian Costume" and other works. I think these works can quite represent the works of Guangzhou. They also pay great attention to skills like the authors in Shanghai, so they have been studying for less than a year, and some skills are already very impressive. They are very free in choosing themes, but this freedom has exceeded a certain limit; for example, themes like "Egyptian Costume" are meaningless. There is also a serious problem, that is, the authors do not have a definite worldview. For example, Li Hua's "Rest of the Hoeing Workers" shows that a hoeing worker is so tired from work that he does not even have the opportunity to sit down for a while, and can only rest on the hoe handle. Doesn't this clearly show how hard our authors are trying to shout for the masses? However, when we look at his "Harvest", it is different. Our author is not concerned about the total collapse of the rural economy in the country and the poor situation of the peasants struggling in the environment of hunger and cold, but instead obliterates the facts to depict the picture of the peasants' abundant harvest. Isn't this a clear expression of the author's inner contradictions? In Peiping, I heard that several authors initiated a national woodcut exhibition in November, and prepared to hold a mobile exhibition in Peiping, Tianjin, Nanjing, Shanghai and other places in January this year. Although we have not seen their works yet, their efforts can be imagined.

3. Publications. In the past year, there have been as many as five or six woodcut collections alone. The Weiming Woodcut Research Society has published four or five books, such as Weiming Woodcut Collection, Liu Xianxinbo Woodcut Collection, etc. The Modern Woodcut Society has also published one book. The content of Liu Xian's woodcut paintings is very empty, and the skills are not mature. Landscapes, animals, etc. account for the majority. He is so busy publishing collections, we can see how impatient the author is in the study of woodcuts. But his efforts are worthy of our admiration. According to the author, it is a hand-printed original, and the first edition printed 150 copies, which took a lot of energy and time to succeed. The Weiming Woodcut Collection is a collection of better works by more than a dozen members of the Weiming Woodcut Research Society. The content is more substantial than Liu Xian's woodcut paintings, and the skills are better. I think the other woodcut books are about the same. These are just products in the process of studying skills, and we don't need to describe them in detail. However, we warmly hope that our authors will go deep into the lowest level of society to collect the materials we need in production in addition to the study of skills in the future. In addition, there are also many woodcut paintings scattered in magazines and newspapers. For example, Luo Qingzhen's works are the most in "Literature". Some of his works strongly express distorted consciousness, such as "Han River Boatman", "Three Peasant Women", etc. can be clearly seen. Like the peasant women and boatmen on the screen, the author did not take them as the central theme, but only as embellishments of the scenery, making a rural landscape painting more colorful. Isn't this kind of work a pastime after tea and dinner? No matter how skilled the technique is, it is always irrelevant to us. Zhang Wang's landscape paintings are better than Luo Qingzhen's in terms of skills. It can also be seen how hard our authors are working on the production of landscape paintings. Unfortunately, people who are struggling desperately in a life of hunger and cold cannot spare the leisure to appreciate it - it is inevitable that they will fail the author's enthusiasm. In addition, publications such as "Literary Comics" and "Taibai" are also enthusiastically introducing woodcut art. The achievements of those works are mostly limited to the skill aspect. Our authors should also put in a lot of hard work in terms of content. The "Ah Q Continuous Paintings" in the "Drama Journal" of "China Daily" may have attracted the attention of many people. The entire painting has only eleven pictures. I think it is not enough to express such a complicated story as "The True Story of Ah Q" with only one painting. If we move these eleven things to people who have not read The True Story of Ah Q, then he will definitely feel inexplicable. So it can only be used as an illustration for the article, and it is not successful as an independent continuous painting.

4. Summary. The facts have shown how rapid the development of Chinese woodcut art has been in the past year. However, this development is very scattered and unsystematic. In the future, we should step up our efforts so that it can embark on a certain track to develop. Only in this way will the future of the Chinese woodcut movement be promising!

Chinese Education in the Past Year 334

— Ge Shixiong

The education cause is a constant activity with no end and no full score. In the past year, there are several points about Chinese education that are worth writing about: Regarding ordinary education: one is the advocacy of production education and labor education, the second is the rise of the call for the reform of the education system, the third is the connection between the national rejuvenation movement and education, and the fourth is the efforts of people from all walks of life for popular education; regarding higher education: one is the increasingly serious problem of "graduation means unemployment", and the second is the fragility of university education reflected by the ban on dancing. The details are described below:

(1) Advocacy of Production Education and Labor Education

Since our country advocated running schools in the late Qing Dynasty, due to the errors in the education policy, it is still a consistent scholar-official education. Students who enter school to study become a special class without living skills. The more people who read books, the fewer producers. For decades, the effect of education has not only failed to help the country embark on the road of production and education, but has also gradually reduced the number of productive elements. Recently, in view of the failure of this kind of bookworm education, there has been the advocacy of "production education" and "labor education" that "uses both hands and brains". According to the reports in various newspapers on July 28, the content is: schools in various places should formulate education policies separately by administrative organs and education organs according to the needs of the local area and the personality and family conditions of the students, and the principle of paying attention to education production should be the principle, and the implementation methods are instructed as follows: (1) Each school must set up a school garden, supervise the students to cultivate by themselves, practice various crops on the spot, and may set up agricultural farms or forest and animal husbandry farms according to the organization of the cooperative, and teachers and students will lead the students to plant and raise livestock, and strictly implement the semi-work and semi-study doctrine. All income, except for expenses and payment for the purchase or lease of land prices, teachers and students are entitled to distribute benefits to encourage them. (2) Each school must set up a specimen room to lead students to collect local natural products or artificial products for display and observation. (3) Add knowledge of various cooperatives to the civic education class, add local products and methods to be improved to the geography class, add various knowledge of agriculture, forestry, sericulture, chicken raising, pig raising, and beekeeping to the natural science class, improve skills, and add methods to improve local industries and manufacture products for sale to the physics and chemistry and manual labor classes to promote them. (4) Advocate diligence and thrift, and cultivate the atmosphere of enduring hardship and not using school servants. (5) Each place must run at least one vocational school according to local needs, so that schools become factories and students become apprentices, and occupations become socialized. It can be said that production education has concrete methods in addition to theoretical advocacy. In December, the Ministry of Education held a national labor achievement exhibition, and the products displayed in various places have indeed exceeded the scope of "handicraft" and "craft". In addition, the National Vocational Education Conference also made many resolutions to assist the implementation of production education, only depending on how it is implemented.

(2) The Call for Reform of the Education System

China's education system has never had its own主張, sometimes imitating Japan, sometimes imitating the United States, sometimes imitating England and France, blind people and blind horses, with nowhere to go. After the Republic of China in 1928, it gradually got on track, and primary and secondary schools have made rapid progress, but it still cannot meet the needs of the country. Therefore, Jiang Menglin, president of Peking University, and Hu Shi, Wu Junsheng, Weng Wenhao, Tao Menghe, Xu Bingchang, Zhou Binglin and others proposed to use experimental methods to revise the education system. The shortcomings of the current education system they found are as follows:

(1) The current primary and secondary school system overemphasizes the aspect of entering higher education, but in fact, the majority of students cannot enter higher education. (3) The current education system cannot take into account both urban and rural areas, making them develop together. In recent years, rural areas have gone bankrupt and the foundation of the country has been shaken, so we must first seek rural construction, and education must first cultivate knowledgeable farmers. (3) Our country's education system and curriculum often copy foreign countries, which are not in line with the national conditions and the special needs of our country. (4) The basic knowledge training of secondary education cannot meet the needs of universities.

After Jiang and others' reform plan was put forward, educators across the country paid great attention to it, believing that it was the beginning and awakening of the reform of the education system, but it is still impossible to say whether this strategy is the only panacea for treating the morbid state of our country's education.

(3) The Connection Between the National Rejuvenation Movement and Education

The death of nationalists and the bankruptcy of rural areas year after year have made the vitality of our nation faltering, and the national rejuvenation movement has been sung into the clouds. In the past, King Goujian of Yue spent ten years gathering and ten years teaching, and finally destroyed Wu. Therefore, in addition to striving for military national defense construction, he has also attached the same importance to spiritual national defense construction. What is spiritual national defense construction? It is national rejuvenation education. Mr. Zheng Tonghe published an article "On National Native Education" in "Jiangsu Education", which is the most acute 주장. In primary schools, the infusion of local teaching materials, national salvation teaching materials, and the importance of civic training in various subjects in the past year, the national rejuvenation movement has been closely linked with education in the subtle influence, which cannot but be said to be a characteristic of education in this year.

(4) The Efforts of People from All Walks of Life for Popular Education

The number of illiterate people in our country is the highest in the world. The level of national intelligence is most closely related to the strength of the country, so the danger of the Chinese nation is not without reason. The call for popular education and improving national intelligence has long been sung into the clouds, but the national treasury is empty, and the education funds have no room for generous planning. Beyond the possible limit, there is no way to expand. In mid-September last year, Ma Xiangbo, Tao Zhixing and others initiated the organization of the China Popular Education Assistance Association. There are two points worth noting about the association: (1) The purpose of the association is to adopt the most economical, fastest, most sustainable, and most progressive methods to strive for the popularization of education needed by the public and children to improve their lives to assist in the creation of the Republic of China and the Datong world. (2) The educational purpose of the association is to develop basic education for the people, to help everyone learn to read and understand, to implement the near elimination of illiteracy, to enhance the ability of production and self-reliance, to improve the lives of the people, and to inspire national consciousness in order to achieve the purpose of self-sufficiency, self-defense, love for the community, and love for the country.

The most important work is the equipment of education vehicles and the plan of mobile schools. Education vehicles are being piloted in the experimental area of the large field and the rural areas near the Zhao Jia Garden Flower Village experimental area in Zhabei, and the results are very good. Each car is staffed by two "little teachers" as teachers. Mobile schools are work-study in nature and have not yet been seen in all matters.

(5) The Increasingly Serious Problem of "Graduation Means Unemployment"

In July of this year, the Beiping University Graduates' Career Movement Alliance suddenly appeared in newspapers. University students are outstanding members of society. At a time when China's construction cause is just beginning and there is an urgent need for talents, it is heard that "graduation means unemployment", which is indeed a complicated and serious problem. Tan Shuzai of the alliance said at a reception for reporters: "... The reason why we have this organization is to promote the improvement of political education and the solution of career problems." The alliance's declaration also said: "For thirty years, the government and people from all walks of life have only known to set up schools and create talents, but no one has asked about how to arrange statistics. Some even regard education as a business, regard students as commodities, and indiscriminately manufacture them, regardless of sales, resulting in more people than positions, and the study is not used. What is used is not what is learned... There are countless people who die in the window. Those who are good at drilling and relying on power and profit can get promoted and gain power... To this day, it has become a society full of unemployment... In a word, it is the career problem, and the influence of bad education." It can be said that he speaks with emotion. After the start of this movement, first Beijing and Hankou responded, and then representatives were sent to Beijing to petition, and the situation became increasingly serious. The comments on this matter in the field of discussion are different. In all fairness, the occurrence of this movement should not be blamed solely on educators. The defects of the political and socio-economic system are the background for its production. However, those who run or preside over university education should be aware of the current crisis of education and have something to change it.

(6) The Fragility of University Education Reflected by the Ban on Dancing

The ban on university students dancing in Shanghai's education sector followed the occupational movement alliance. "Dancing" itself cannot be regarded as an evil, but university students are accustomed to the pleasures of sensual entertainment, obsessed with forgetting to return, and putting the pursuit of academics and the discipline of life behind them, which is enough to make university education fundamentally bankrupt. However, whether banning dancing can drive students into the study room, and whether banning dancing can prevent students from being superstitious in other sensual pleasures, we cannot help but be deeply suspicious of this.

The ban on dancing in various universities in Shanghai is precisely a reflection of the unfulfillingness of current university life, the lack of active training, and the thin atmosphere of academic research. Therefore, banning dancing is not a fundamental solution, and banning dancing may not have good results. If the hosts of the university do not start from improving the facilities, enriching the curriculum, and making the idle spirit of university students get proper catharsis, I have not seen the palliative measure of banning dancing.

In summary, Chinese education in the past year can be said to be advancing steadily in the process of awakening, repentance, and transformation from any aspect. Perhaps shortcomings can be found everywhere, but the consistent attitude of people in the education sector to seek good is always admirable. The old year has passed, and the author finally wishes the workers in the education cause to create a new page in the history of education in the new year!

The Chinese Book Industry Over the Past Year 335

— By Kang Nai-de

The fireball of recession continues to roll through the market, incinerating the prosperity of various industries and businesses. The book industry, while also a cultural endeavor, cannot escape the misfortune befalling general industries and businesses. The phenomenon of recession was even more pronounced in the Chinese book industry in 1934.

As everyone knows, the buyers of books are generally intellectuals, especially young students. However, in recent years, due to the decline of industry and commerce and the bankruptcy of the rural economy, many intellectuals and young students have been plunged into unemployment and lack of schooling amidst the disaster of unemployment panic. They even have trouble affording breadsticks and soy milk for rent, so where would they have money to buy books? As a result, the purchasing power for books has decreased, and the business of bookstores has naturally declined day by day.

According to general booksellers, the major book markets in China have always been: Shanghai, Beijing, Northeast China, Nanjing, Guangdong, Fujian, Sichuan... and other places. But what about now? The Northeast has already been forcibly occupied by Japan, and Chinese books simply cannot be transported there for sale, which goes without saying. As for other places, the book market is not what it used to be and is very bleak and deserted. Now, let's first look at Beijing—

The "book market" in Beijing is mainly in the Dong'an Market and Xidan Shopping Center. General booksellers run small shops or set up stalls of various sizes in these two places to conduct their business. In the past, in addition to selling books from bookstores in Shanghai, they also secretly reprinted books that were easy to sell at low prices to obtain greater profits. Later, because it aroused serious interference from publishers and authors, the so-called "pirated books in Beijing" gradually decreased. Now, their business mainly consists of selling books published by various bookstores in Shanghai and selling books bought cheaply from poor students. However, because of the decrease in the purchasing power of books, the "book market" in Beijing is far from as lively as it used to be, and many book stalls no longer exist.

Next is Nanjing—According to the "Xu Bao" newspaper: "The bookstore industry in Nanjing was insignificant before the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928). However, since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, the bookstore industry has developed in response to the needs of the times. It was not until the winter of the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931) that the Nanjing Bookstore Trade Association was established to guide the development of the industry. Until recently, 85 companies have joined the association for cooperation... The business of the bookstore industry in Nanjing has reached its peak in recent years. In this autumn of recession, almost every bookstore is losing money. The reasons are: (1) Each bookstore has an excessive inventory of books. In order to seek economic activity, most small and medium-sized bookstores sell them off at a loss, such as setting a price of one yuan, then giving a 10% discount, and then a 90% discount. They do not listen to the association's restrictions, which makes it impossible to standardize book prices. (2) In Shanghai, although there is a book publishing review committee to review published books, the bookstores in this city do not know which books are prohibited due to a lack of information. They casually buy them from Shanghai and are prohibited from selling them when they arrive in Beijing, resulting in unexpected losses." Why do bookstores have "excessive inventories of books"? And why do they "sell off at a loss"? The answer is very simple: because the market is sluggish, few people buy books, and there is no other way but to do so!

The situation in other places such as Guangdong and Sichuan is the same. In the past, many bookstores in Guangzhou, Chengdu, and other places had commission agents in Shanghai who regularly purchased books from bookstores in Shanghai. However, now not only are some commission agents gone, but many bookstores have also closed their doors, losing their existence altogether. Therefore, bookstores in Shanghai do not know how many book debts they cannot recover in these places.

Shanghai is undoubtedly the center of the Chinese book industry, and most bookstores in other places sell books published by various bookstores in Shanghai. Because of the sluggishness of the entire market and the poor business of bookstores everywhere, the business of various bookstores in Shanghai, as the center of the book industry, is of course a big problem. Under these circumstances, bookstores in Shanghai, in order to survive, have to compete with each other. This phenomenon of competition is manifested in the publishing trends and general business methods of various bookstores.

In the Chinese publishing industry in 1934, we can see two major trends: one is that some small bookstores, because they cannot publish books in large quantities, can only rely on publishing magazines to maintain appearances; the other is that the larger bookstores, because they see that the purchasing power for general books has decreased and cannot promote sales, desperately reprint ancient books such as complete works and complete histories, with libraries, cultural institutions, and historical experts as their main customers. The result of the former trend is the creation of the name "Magazine Year"; the manifestation of the latter trend reveals a characteristic of the retro trend.

At the same time, with the development of the retro trend, there are also people who, because their economic strength is weak and they cannot follow "Commercial Press" and "Zhonghua Book Company" to reprint large quantities of ancient Chinese books, but also want to seize the opportunity of retro, and have no other way, so they desperately transport Western antiques. For example, Xin Ken Bookstore specializes in publishing antiques of Western European philosophy and science from the 17th and 18th centuries, and even the Greek era, to complement the "Siku Quanshu" ("Complete Library of the Four Treasures"), "Gujin Tushu Jicheng" ("Complete Collection of Illustrations and Writings from the Earliest to Current Times"), "Twenty-Five Histories"... and other national quintessences. However, unfortunately, new books of all kinds still have their buyers, and Chinese ancient books are also taken care of by libraries, cultural institutions, and those historical experts. Only these Western antiques, which have been criticized and sorted out by many great thinkers, are simply ignored. Therefore, the result of these speculators' speculation is not only unable to make their business prosper, but also creates a greater crisis in business. The problem is that there are no buyers, which leads to an increase in inventory, a lack of cash flow, and the inability to deal with general creditors.

As for general business methods, the competition among bookstores in Shanghai is also clearly manifested. Take "big price cuts" as an example. What we see is: today Bookstore A publishes an advertisement selling books at an 80% discount of the original price, and tomorrow Bookstore B will sell books at a 50% discount. Then, on the book market, there are cries of "30% discount", "40% discount"... and so on. If you are willing to go to the bookstores on Fourth Horse Road to take a look, then you will definitely see words such as "New books are sold as cheap goods," "One yuan sells for only eight cents," "How much does a pound of new books cost?" (Books have become rice and flour and must be measured in pounds!) and "Books are sold at a 10% discount and then an 80% discount," etc. At the same time, some bookstores, such as "Life Bookstore" and "Kaiming Bookstore," have even more advertisements, saying that out-of-town customers who purchase books from them can avoid remittance fees. And "Shanghai Magazine Company," after its opening, its "first cry" was: "Take unlimited responsibility to subscribe to magazines for you," "If there is a suspension of publication midway, you can take back the order from this company."... Such competition is probably unique in recent years.

In the mutual competition of bookstores, those with strong capital can of course participate in the competition and maintain appearances, but small bookstores with weak economic strength cannot survive. It is said that there are one or two small bookstores that owe too much money to printing houses and paper shops and cannot support themselves, and they are afraid that they will close down.

As a result of the recession in the book industry, the printing industry and the paper industry will naturally be affected. At the same time, the lives of general literati have also been greatly affected. It is very obvious that because books do not sell well, it is not easy to sell the manuscripts of literati. Even if they are sold, because the selling price is too low and the relationships of "discounts," "removing blank spaces," "removing punctuation," and even "removing foreign languages" (this is a new invention of a certain big bookseller recently!), the result of the literati spending a lot of time and racking their brains is very little; moreover, there is also a kind of bookseller who specializes in defrauding manuscripts, taking the translations of literati and printing them into books, and refusing to give them royalties or royalties. I have a friend who translated a book and published it in a small bookstore. Now the book has been reprinted, but he has not received a penny of royalties. When he recently went to the bookstore to ask for royalties, the booksellers actually joked with him: Haha! Your book was originally sent to us for publication, there are no royalties! Thank you! As a result, this friend had no choice but to grit his teeth, feel pain in his heart, and blame his "fate for being unfortunate!"—Such ridiculous things also happen! From this, we can imagine the disasters suffered by the general literati in the recession of the book industry.

The Chinese Publishing Industry Over the Past Year 336

— By Ms. Fan Pu

The development and changes of culture have time and space. In a certain era, based on a certain spatial environment, the trend and content of a certain cultural thought are embodied, which is almost a fact that does not need to be mentioned. Naturally, to understand the content and trend of the thought and culture of a certain era, we must observe it from both the author and the reader to see through its full form. However, there is also a simple method that can be used as an indicator for our testing, that is, to see the situation of the publishing industry. Of course, the psychology of the majority of people in the society, what the author wants to say, and what books and newspapers the readers love to read and require are in contradiction with the publishing industry. Because many authors write things that publishing institutions often do not want, so they cannot be published, and the knowledge and the books and newspapers that many readers need are not provided by the publishing industry. Therefore, to accurately explore the depths of social thought and understand its trends, this cannot be simply seen from the current situation of the publishing industry. Even so, the expression of social thought in a certain era, which becomes a characteristic of the cultural trend, and can be used as a material for understanding the present and the future, can also be seen from the expression of the publishing industry and used as a criterion for evaluation. Because the publishing industry can generally reflect the social environment. What it can publish is determined by the social environment. What works it can obtain for publication can also show what stage the social culture of this era has progressed to and what exploration achievements have been obtained. As for the sales of its publications, it is even more sufficient to explain the readers' requirements and tendencies. In a word, all of this embodies the content and trends of the entire society's thought, culture, and even politics and economy. Therefore, when we review the situation of the Chinese publishing industry over the past year, it is tantamount to reviewing the entire cultural development stage of China over the past year, especially hoping that readers will see it as a symbol of the history of Chinese thought over the past year.

Although the number of books in the Chinese publishing industry in 1934 was not necessarily more than in 1928 and 1929, it always exceeded that of 1915 to 1927. In terms of magazines, we are sure that it cannot catch up with 1925 to 1927 in terms of quantity, but last year can indeed be said to be a magazine year. According to the statistics provided to us by Mr. Shu Xincheng in the Cultural Construction Monthly, from 1928 to 1931, 1,000 kinds of books were registered in the Ministry of Internal Affairs, 886 kinds in 1932, and 1,890 kinds in 1933, totaling 3,776 kinds. In terms of magazines and newspapers, there were 1,403 kinds from September 1928 to December 1932, 1,919 kinds in 1933, totaling 3,331 kinds. And from January to September 1934, only 654 kinds of newspapers and magazines were registered in the Ministry of Internal Affairs. According to the statistics in Shen Bao's advertisements, the total number of newly published publications up to October was only 1,286 kinds, and he did not distinguish between books, newspapers, and magazines. Therefore, 1934 seems to be far behind 1933. But these numbers are not very accurate. Because from 1928 to 1932, most of the books were not registered. The actual number should be far above the registered number. And in 1934, even including books and magazines, it is still not enough according to Shen Bao's advertisements. Because most of the advertisements in Shen Bao are limited to publications in Beijing and Shanghai, and most of the publications in Tianjin, Beijing, Guangzhou, and other places are advertised in local newspapers, so that number is far from enough to summarize the whole country. Therefore, according to the general estimation of referring to the facts, from 1925 to 1927, there were few books and many magazines, and in the three or four years after 1928, more books were published and fewer magazines were published. In 1934, the number of books was less than in the previous period, but it was not particularly behind. It was just that the direction had changed somewhat. As for magazines, they were much more developed than after 1928.

What are the reasons for this change in the publishing industry? Generally speaking, it is because 1925 to 1927 was a period of action. In that era, most people spent all their time and energy on action, and they did not have time to do in-depth research. What they needed was only simple and realistic propaganda and practical guidance. Therefore, few people read entire books. At that time, not only did activists need propaganda and brief realistic action guidance, but also social organizations were particularly developed. Each school had several or more organizations, and each organization mostly had its own publications. In society, there were also many general organizations and publications. These are all the reasons why book publishing could not keep up with the development of magazines in that era. But after 1928, the period of widespread action passed, and the activities of social organizations also decreased. The tendency of static research gradually replaced dynamic activities. The deepening of theory and knowledge, and the reflection on past historical events cannot be satisfied by simple magazines. Therefore, the number of magazines gradually decreased later, and the introduction of books, especially theoretical books of basic knowledge, became developed in those years. Many small new culture bookstores that sprang up like mushrooms after the rain in those years were enough to express the characteristics of the publishing industry at that time. As the era moved to 1934, due to the determination of objective circumstances, the theoretical introduction and research of social sciences encountered difficulties. Therefore, the publishing direction since 1928 could no longer continue as before, and this also affected the book publishing aspect. However, the static state of the era has not only not changed, but has also deepened more and more. Therefore, research is still an objectively required condition. So the quantity of book publications in 1934 did not show a special decline, but only the direction showed a clear change from the past. As for magazines, there are many reasons to decide its activity in objective causes. First, because there were two kinds of thought competing fiercely in this year, one in the offensive, in order to win complete leadership and replace it, worked hard to publish its magazines as propaganda weapons. But what about the side being attacked? It is still unwilling to show weakness, often changing its style and content at any time to try to maintain its position, and constantly publishing magazines. Second, the current China is in a period of national crisis. Everyone is in a state of bewilderment and anxiety. There are indeed endless practical problems in front of us, making everyone feel that they cannot ignore them and must study and understand them. But magazines are relatively easy to express opinions, because those short essays can still vaguely and partially reveal some opinions. Therefore, the large number of magazines in 1934 precisely shows that Chinese society has formed a social depression and complaint phenomenon that it has to say a few words because the crisis is urgent. Third, the world and China's recession has made ordinary intellectuals unemployed and impoverished, and the decline of the new book industry has made their last way out of eating written food increasingly narrow. Therefore, everyone flocks to running magazines as a way to find a way out for themselves, solve temporary life, and even recruit unemployed literati as a basis for activities. So the special development of magazines this year is also enough to explain the inside of the intellectual's life panic. In short, the publishing industry in 1934 formed its first characteristic of being a magazine year because of the above-mentioned reasons.

It has already been proposed above that the publishing industry in 1934 has changed its direction. This is not only a problem that can be proposed, but also a characteristic of the publishing industry this year. Because in the past publishing industry, the trend of books was towards the discussion and introduction of general principles and principles of social sciences. But this kind of discussion and introduction is contradictory to the environment at the present time, and it has to be stopped. Therefore, two universal new tendencies have occurred in the publishing industry in terms of publishing books. On the one hand, old antiques have reappeared: the most obvious is the reprint of the Siku Treasures by the Commercial Press, with two or three hundred and one kinds in the first collection alone, totaling about two thousand boats; the Zhonghua Book Company's abridged edition of Gujin Tushu Jicheng, about 800 volumes; the Song Qisha Tibetan Sutra 592 volumes, and the Four Series, Four Essentials, Wanwei Bie Collection, and Liaohai Series are all being printed. In addition, there are also many small bookstores and social organizations that reprint old books. Therefore, if it is right to say that 1934 is a magazine year, then we can also call it a year of the re-emergence of old books and antiques. On the other hand, although there are relatively few practical theoretical research and introductions for the publication of books, in addition to re-releasing domestic old goods, there is also a new atmosphere of introducing philosophy and science from abroad. The Commercial Press has recently selected many famous world philosophy and science works for translation. The Sun Yat-sen Culture and Education Center has published many such books in the first issue, and the second issue is also selecting and translating famous philosophy and science works. Xin Ken Bookstore has already published many philosophy and science series, and is still continuing to translate them. Therefore, the publishing industry in 1934 can be said to be a year of theoretical and practical science introduction. In particular, theoretical natural science in natural science introduced many kinds of world-famous masterpieces in this year. The former tendency is to run back to the old road. The negative effect on the progress of Chinese thought and culture will have a temporary impact, which is undeniable. In the latter, we must not underestimate it, thinking that it has gone out of the practice circle and has no many benefits. It must be known that in China, the profound understanding and understanding of nature has always been backward. The ultimate problem of mankind is the problem of dealing with nature. The correct understanding of nature will become the starting point of correct philosophical thinking, and can promote the birth of the correct outlook on life, form the correct social outlook, and reach the correct practical theory. In this way, these introductions of philosophy and science are precisely indicating that the Chinese ideological circle is making further efforts to deeply understand the entire world. In the near future, a Chinese ideological renaissance will be led by the progress of natural science to achieve social restoration. Therefore, the change in the direction of the publishing industry in 1934 is to express its second characteristic with the contradictory phenomenon of old book reprints and scientific introductions running in opposite directions.

Secondly, judging from the situation of the publishing industry in 1934, on the one hand, it can prove that China's current economic situation is recession and the poverty of the general public is increasing. On the other hand, the cultural movement has further reduced its universality, and it shows that most young people do not like to read books and do not seek further education. Only a few people are working hard on the aforementioned research on philosophy and natural science. We can get proof of these phenomena from many facts. First, although there were still a considerable number of books published throughout 1934, the purchase of old books was mostly based on cultural institutions such as school libraries as employers. The sales of new philosophy and science were also very bad, and very few people bought them. All bookstores often have big sales, and even the big bookstores such as Commercial Press and Zhonghua, which have never been discounted, have joined the big sale competition, and some bookstores have big sales all year round, and even have discounts of 10% or 20%. However, despite such fierce price competition, the result is still poor business, and many bookstores cannot maintain themselves. This precisely shows the phenomenon that the people are poor and unable to buy books to read, or that many wealthy young students are unwilling to read books. Second, boring novels and pictorials with fleshiness sell better than serious books. When a newspaper publishes sufficient news about sports and movies, people rush to buy it. This shows that most young people are mentally bored and depraved, do not take academics seriously, and are wholeheartedly indulging in boring pastimes. In fact, the special popularity of magazines and the best-selling

(The following continues on page 5)

Page 22

Page 23

of essays, in which there is also the tendency of most people to not be willing to seek further education. Although it is not to say that reading magazines is wrong, nor is it to say that essay publications are completely meaningless, it is precisely a symbol of the reader's simple calculations on economics and understanding problems. Therefore, the mentality of casually buying one or two magazines or essays and looking at them is fully revealed. All of the above-mentioned phenomena are the third characteristic of the culture in 1934 embodied in the publishing industry.

Furthermore, in terms of the content of publications in 1934, we have already said in the front that books are characterized by the simultaneous development of the trend towards dazzling antiques and the introduction of philosophy and science. However, in terms of magazines, there is also a clear tendency that can be identified. Most magazines only focus on the study of international politics on political issues, and mostly focus on the analysis of international economic panic and the collapse of China's rural economy and the decline of the city economy on economic issues. There is a great tendency to not explore the issues of China's national independence and freedom. This is just like the prevalence of essays and humorous writing in 1934. It is also one of the characteristics of the publishing industry.

In summary, the overview of the publishing industry in 1934 embodies the phenomenon of both advantages and disadvantages in the Chinese ideological circle and cultural movement. On the one hand, it is the extreme development of ideological differentiation. On the other hand, it shows the general recession, so most people are gradually eliminated from the knowledge circle and cannot receive the grace of publishing culture. The general youth's weariness of learning and the decline and stagnation of the new book industry are also serious problems. We hope that in 1935, the baptism of science will be popularized in the general society, and this will save the decline of the new book industry. That is the fortune of China's cultural future and the fortune of the Chinese nation.

The Esperanto Movement in China Over the Past Year 337

— Bing

The Esperanto movement in China is a wing of the global Esperanto movement, just as China is a link in the world. Therefore, when reviewing the Esperanto movement in China over the past year, it is necessary to simultaneously look back at the international Esperanto movement.

The past year was a turbulent year politically, and similarly, it was an eventful year for the international Esperanto movement. In the past year, various characters have appeared on the stage of the international Esperanto movement. Some even used the banner of so-called "neutralism" (advocating a conservative neutral attitude towards religion and politics) to attract audiences, but because these actors themselves had long lost the enthusiasm of idealism, the result was just a chorus of boos from the audience. Some put on the clothing of dead people, acting as brown propagandists. Some played with beautiful lines to fool honest people. The humorous school with "Pirate" as its trademark, and the news reporter faction ("Nia Gazeto" faction) which flaunts collectivism, also appeared on stage in 1934. Truly, a star-studded gathering, how lively!

But, what events in the international Esperanto movement over the past year are particularly worth mentioning? Well, let's not join the crowd and calmly examine it—

First is the Esperanto movement under Mr. Hitler's rule. Since Hitler came to power, Esperanto has been regarded as a "Jewish creation" and rejected. So those neutralist gentlemen were so scared that they dared not even mention neutralism. It turns out that neutralism is the "third kind of person," and in present-day Germany, you are not allowed to fall in the middle. So a whole group of neutralists came wearing brown uniforms. This completely exposed the "neutralist peep show." But they said that Esperanto and the "internal idea" (the ideal of human love advocated by Zamenhof) were originally two different things and irrelevant. In this way, the "internal idea" has become an "external idea." However, in Germany, there is another miracle. The GLEA (German Workers' Esperanto Association), which has been banned for a long time, has not disappeared, and is still engaged in research with difficulty. When the IPE (International of Workers Esperantists) held a congress in France last August, the GLEA officially sent more than ten representatives, bringing with them 500 marks donated by the GLEA to the IPE, and attended the congress in a grand manner.

Second is the IPE after its departure. Since the IPE's headquarters in Germany was sealed, it moved to the Netherlands and began to reorganize. By last year's congress, it had almost returned to its original state. Branches in various countries have cooperated with workers' Esperanto speakers belonging to other international organizations in international communication research, and have achieved considerable success. Some workers' Esperanto groups in Hungary and other countries have announced their separation from SAT (World Anational Association, also a workers' Esperanto international organization) and joined the IPE. On the other hand, SAT cadres are still insisting on strange theories such as "colonial people are not happy to be liberated," "it is not unreasonable for other ethnic groups to develop resources that cannot be developed by the local ethnic group," aren't they indirectly supporting imperialism? Many SAT members are eagerly hoping to cooperate with the IPE, which can be seen from the resolution passed at last year's SAT congress to reunify the workers' Esperanto movement.

Third is the new trend of the Soviet Esperanto movement. In recent years, with the pace of industrial construction, the Soviet Union has been vigorously carrying out the education of worker internationalism, and Esperanto has been widely used. Especially among children, in the so-called Young Pioneers, a lively Esperanto movement is being carried out. Here, let me give a concrete fact. In a primary school in the Azerbaijan Republic of Transcaucasia, a team of young people used Esperanto to communicate with the world and all ethnic groups in the Soviet Union. The children designated one person from each country as an "ambassador," responsible for collecting materials from that country and conducting very broad and interesting communication. As a result, in last year's All-Soviet Children's International Communication Competition, they won the best result—first place. So the children were sent to travel all over the Soviet Union, and also sent to Moscow to receive awards. At the award ceremony, the Soviet Esperanto Union also sent someone to give a public speech. On the way back, more than thirty representatives of various groups accompanied these children home, but on the way, these adults all swore that they would definitely learn Esperanto from now on. This fact tells us what kind of future Esperanto will have.

In addition, there are many, many events worth mentioning in the international Esperanto movement. Here we can only mention the following: (1) Publishing activities—a novel with the hero Chapajev of the Soviet Civil War era as the protagonist (translated from Russian), Dante's "Inferno" (it is said that the translator learned the original text in order to translate this masterpiece), "Esperanto Encyclopedia," "Pick Up the Gun" (a novel depicting the life of the Soviet army), "Whither Goest Thou" (translated by Zamenhof's daughter), "City of Towers" (an original novel depicting the unemployment panic in Austria)... "Chemical Industry" (monthly magazine, compiled and printed by Soviet chemical workers Esperantists), "Soviet School" (compiled and printed by Soviet educators Esperantists), "Our Newspaper" (newspaper-type monthly magazine), "Pirate" humorous monthly magazine)... (2) New groups—"Saar-Alsace-Lorraine Workers' Esperanto Association" (publishes two kinds of publications); "International Progressive Esperanto Educators' Federation," publishes the organ "Educators' Torch" and "Worldwide Esperanto Education Communication." (3) Trends of IAREV—"International Association of Revolutionary Esperanto Writers" (IAREV) publishes the organ "Mass Literature," and plans to publish literary correspondence, assist writers from various countries, collect data from all over the world, and translate (full or excerpt translation) various masterpieces—customized translation.

Now let's turn back and take a look at the domestic situation: How much progress has the Esperanto movement in China made in the past year?

First is the progress in propaganda. Today's young Esperanto speakers are no longer like our predecessors, who treat Esperanto worship as a panacea for world peace, saying that Esperanto is easy to learn, grammar has only sixteen rules, and shutting their mouths world is the same, human being is a family. It is not enough to use ease to publicize, and utopian preaching is even more harmful to obscuring reality. We can only show the true meaning of Esperanto and gain more supporters in concrete and practical work, in participating in activities that help society and culture. From this understanding, the propaganda work has achieved a part of it. Just talking about the item of literal propaganda, we no longer easily find those beautiful and poisonous phrases like a fool talking in his sleep. And in various important newspapers and periodicals in China, there are often texts about Esperanto and works translated from Esperanto. For example, in "Shen Bao", "Shen Bao Monthly", "China Daily", "China Monthly", "Literature", "Literature Quarterly", "Reader", "Modern", "Youth World", "Tai Bai", "World Knowledge",... there have been such texts. On the one hand, this shows the efforts of the Esperanto speakers themselves, and on the other hand, it is also because the editors and the general readers have a deeper understanding of Esperanto. We believe that this kind of propaganda method (naturally, the significance of this work is not only propaganda) is legitimate.

Second is the development of the movement. With the expansion of propaganda, the movement has indeed made some new progress in the past year. In the Esperanto circle, there are currently many new Esperanto speakers—new people are beginning to appear. From another perspective, this is also the improvement of general language skills. One year ago, even half a year ago, some people who had just started reading the alphabet were already able to use Esperanto to debate and converse, and were already able to use Esperanto to read, write letters, write essays, and translate. From the perspective of the overall trend of the movement, it has also begun to step onto a brand-new stage, namely the popularization of Esperanto. Esperanto has not only entered schools, but also entered stores, factories, and rural areas. In the inland Esperanto movement, new groups have been established in Guizhou, Jing County, Hebei, and other places. There are also more or less developments in Peiping, Qingdao, Tianjin, Guangzhou, Taiyuan, Nanjing, Changsha, and Chengdu. Here we will not go into details due to space limitations. The "Shanghai Esperanto Association," which has a long history, was destroyed in Zhabei during the January 28 Incident. Since its revival the year before last, we have been hoping that it can work hard for the future of our language. Unfortunately, it suddenly stagnated in 1934, and the monthly magazine "Green Light" was also discontinued. This has to be said to be a pity.

Third is the expansion of the scope of work. For the sake of practical Esperanto, the inevitable result is that Esperanto speakers work separately in various fields, which is what I want to say here about the expansion of the scope of work. The movement in the past year has paid attention to this point. Today's Esperanto speakers have felt that a single Esperanto movement is not enough. What is important is the movement of applying Esperanto. Therefore, the communication movement in the past year has been a little more active than the previous year. Other examples include the research on language theory, the translation of literary works, the translation of foreign correspondence, and so on.

Fourth is the mass language debate. The participation of Esperanto speakers in the mass language debate, as well as the enthusiasm and concern for this issue in the Esperanto central mass language discussion, are worth special mention. In particular, the Latinization of Chinese calligraphy has received support from Chinese Esperanto speakers. In this debate, it shows that modern Chinese Esperanto speakers are no longer those unrealistic dreamers who do not eat human food and despise the national language, but the most practical workers in the language garden. They want to organically link the international language movement and the reform movement of the national language. This is a major event in the Esperanto world in 1934.

In terms of publishing, all places are still sluggish due to economic difficulties. The more important publications in the past year include: Esperanto Reader (Shanghai Esperanto Bookstore), Plena Votaro (Comprehensive Bookstore Reprinted), Petro (Elementary Textbook, Comprehensive Bookstore Reprinted), Chinese Esperanto Dictionary (Peiping), Immensee (Peiping), Salome (Chengdu),... In terms of periodicals, "The World" published in Shanghai is currently the most content-rich publication, and others include "The Sower" in Taiyuan, "The Light of Esperanto" in Peiping, "Guangzhou Esperanto Monthly" in Guangzhou, and Verdemulo, "Green Banner" in Chengdu, and so on.

The Esperanto movement in China has a very promising future. The development of the Esperanto movement of small and weak nations, as Akita Ujaku said, is of great significance to the entire world movement. However, there are still countless difficulties lying in front of the Chinese Esperanto movement, which need to be overcome by us one by one. Esperanto speakers, work hard!

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

The Nature of Newsreels and Their Production (Part 2) 341

— Huang Yingdai

Representing a Page in History Recorded

Value Estimated by Event Changes

No sooner said than done, bullets flew horizontally. George, behind the South King's car, immediately saw two photographers hit by stray bullets and fell down, one already fatally wounded. A timid person would have run away at this time, but he steadied his mind and immediately aimed the camera at the car, capturing every important shot. George felt that his harvest was not enough, so he rushed into the crowd and took many amazing shots inside the South King's car. At this time, the South King's face was already pale and he was dead in the car. Raymond saw the tragedy happen, first recorded all the chaotic noise, and then took a circular shot. The Mackie brothers, they photographed the assassin's weapon, held in the hand of a guard, and also photographed the assassin lying on the ground after being killed by the crowd and the guards. After the tragedy, the chaos of order, the noise of the crowd, everything was captured into the camera and recorded into the microphone.

Photography and sound recording were so dangerous at that time, but their responsibility absolutely could not be avoided. After this newsreel gained an unexpected harvest, it then encountered many difficulties. An airplane, already prepared, wanted to carry the shot film to Paris, organize it in Paris, and then immediately transport it to the Bremen ship to send it to New York, but the representative of the Fox Company was arrested in La Bouget. The film transported from Marseille was all detained because there were orders that films about the Marseille tragedy were not allowed to be transported overseas. Later, after many difficulties and careful consideration by the authorities, all the films were returned, but the stipulated condition was that the film could only be made under the supervision of the French Film Examination Board. After many disputes with the authorities, the shackles were lifted, and the Fox Company immediately transported the films to the Washington ship by plane without stopping. This ship sailed to the United States the next day. Upon arrival in the United States, it was immediately sent to the Hollywood Fox studio by plane. Quickly made this newsreel. During the filming, there were many dangers and difficulties, but it is indeed a valuable record of a page in history. The South King's landing, the car's progress, the assassination, Alexander's remains, Bardou's paleness, everything, is a rare newsreel!

From the above description, we can immediately discover several principles in the nature and production of newsreels.

(1) Newsreels can represent a page in history, and are easier to make a deep impression on people than written records.

(2) The value of newsreels cannot be estimated in advance, and rises or falls depending on the temporary expansion or reduction of the event.

(3) Valuable newsreels can be preserved permanently, so that future generations can see a page in history on the screen and in reality.

(4) When filming newsreels, the work of the staff should be properly allocated in advance.

(5) The filming of newsreels is the sole responsibility of the photographer. Unlike general films, there is a director in charge, and the photographer's responsibility is lighter.

(6) The photographer who shoots newsreels must have a spirit of adventure and courage, so that even if an incident occurs, they can remain calm and collect the film in the chaos. The technique must be quick, and the thinking must be agile, because if a general shot is broken, it can be replaced, and even several can be replaced. The dynamic state of the news disappears in a flash and cannot be replayed once. If the technique is slow, it cannot be captured. What should be included in the shot and what can be abandoned to avoid wasting film must be adapted to the situation.

(7) When many film companies are filming the same newsreel at the same time, they must win by surprise and shoot the film that others don't have time to shoot.

(8) After the film is shot, the transportation and production must be fast, so that it can be released to the public as soon as possible, in order to satisfy the audience's news desire and overwhelm the competition in the same industry. (End)

Movie Talk

Review of "Secret Boudoir" 342

— Ling He

What Every Woman Knows – Nanjing –

The film adaptation of the novel "What Every Woman Knows," which this publication previously translated as "Admonitions for Good Wives," is now being released under the title "Secret Boudoir." The former translation at least managed to convey the content, while the latter, apart from the allure of sensual excitement, seems to lack any other meaning.

The ideology of virtuous mothers and good wives still holds considerable interest among American filmmakers, as demonstrated in works like "Little Women." Now, the play "Secret Boudoir" by J.M. Barrie is being adapted for the screen, continuing to promote this ideology and serving as a stark contrast to the morally decadent modern women.

Regarding the works of the English author Barrie (Sir J.M. Barrie), China has previously seen Hong Shen's translations of "The Second Dream" (a three-act play) and "The Admirable Crichton," among others. "What Every Woman Knows," translated as "Secret Boudoir," was originally a four-act play. His works demonstrate a profound sense of human relationships and worldly experiences, tinged with deep sorrow. He is an aging modern writer whose philosophy and outdated worldview are undoubtedly far removed from reality.

Now, we might as well observe how the playwright presents his theme as a whole, which is most evident in the male protagonist: He is a stubborn man who is diligent and studious. Therefore, despite being a common laborer, he eventually wins a labor party election with the help of others and is appointed to the cabinet. However, he needs a good inner helper to manage his life and assist his career. Thus, the virtuous wife, played by Helen Hayes, appears. A young working-class man, a high-ranking cabinet official, and a virtuous wife who sacrifices herself in various aspects of love to help her husband achieve fame are, in the playwright's view, undoubtedly beneficial to the modern social system.

In terms of the relative importance of the male and female protagonists, the female protagonist's adherence to womanly virtue naturally occupies a major position in the play. However, people will not overlook the question of for whom is the womanly virtue that she expresses, which she believes "every woman should know," actually intended? Considering this connection further reveals the influence of the playwright's old worldview. As for the manipulative tactics used to win the love of her husband, which are frequently seen in American films, they do not hinder the original theme and further glorify the personality of the female protagonist.

Regarding the theme as described above, based on our current understanding, it is adequately expressed cinematically, realizing the theme of the play.

There is a special kind of charm here. In a serene atmosphere, a slight, bitter smile of life is emitted. Especially due to the success of Helen Hayes's acting, particularly in the final scene, the so-called laughter through tears is indeed portrayed quite profoundly. However, this work may feel dull to audiences who only seek pleasure. For example, the laughter is so subtle, and the dialogue is so heavy and tedious. After the climax of the election, the emotionally charged scenes, such as Helen discovering her husband's secrets, are difficult to please the general audience. There is an air of melancholy here, but melancholy is not as popular as unconscious laughter, although there are many humorous scenes.

Another point to mention is that the male lead's speech is very slurred, although his movements show that he has received good basic training. As for Helen Hayes's makeup at the age of twenty-six, it seems a bit old, and the first part is not as natural as the second part, which is not unrelated to her own age.

Audience Opinions

My Views on "Renzhu" 343

— Zhou Hui

After watching "Renzhu," I couldn't help but feel disappointed. I can't believe that at this time when domestic films are making progress, there is still such a regression!

It is very obvious that the author, in order to "cater to the audience's psychology" and for "business reasons," does not hesitate to bring back this vulgar and anachronistic "lily of the valley." This is considered a painful matter.

In terms of performance, "Renzhu" is also a failure. The entire play cannot escape the atmosphere of a civilized drama, and the lengthy dialogues and stiff expressions do not give people a pleasant feeling. The director, in this regard, only achieves a "flat" level, without any clever techniques.

Regarding the actors, Fan Xuepeng is fundamentally a failure, and Chen Qiufeng's unsuitability for the character naturally makes the effort unrewarding. Ye Qiuxin has achieved considerable success.

Finally, it is worth mentioning that the sound in the picture is still clear.

Submission Guidelines for Shenbao Film Supplement 344

This publication is a film publication that promotes culture and art. We welcome submissions from outside sources and will pay generously once they are published.

Once a text is published and paid for, the copyright belongs to Shenbao.

The language of this publication is mainly vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

Each submission must be stamped; otherwise, it will not be paid.

The space in this publication is limited, so the text should be as concise as possible. Each submission should be limited to around 500 words.

If the submission is a translation, the original should be attached. English should be avoided where possible. Texts, photos, etc., will not be returned unless specifically requested in advance and accompanied by return postage.

Movie Anecdotes 345

— Luo Ping

World-renowned director René Clair will go to Hollywood after directing a film for London Film Company. It is rumored that the film he will direct will be entirely in English.

Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer has hired H.M. Harwood as a screenwriter. Harwood is the author of Cynara. The dialogues in "The Private Life of Don Juan" and the screenplay of "The Iron Duke," starring George Arliss in England, are all written by Harwood.

The life of Simon Bolivar, a famous South American revolutionary, has been adopted by Mr.杏那克, the production director of 20th Century Fox, and will be made into a movie.

Famous female director Dorothy Arzner will begin filming a new film, "Working Girls," starring Rose Hobart.

Film Novel

Forsaking All Others (2) 346

— Su Yin

Suddenly, someone knocked on the door outside, knocking urgently. The person who came in after the door opened was none other than the groom himself. He held a silver cocktail shaker in his hand and sang love songs in his mouth. As he sang, he walked to Mary's massage bed. Mary exclaimed, "Baby!" Dillon didn't say a word but frowned at her. After a while, he shrugged his shoulders and said, "Oh, is this pile of mess the woman I'm going to marry?" He then took his hand and smeared some of the ointment from Mary's face onto his nose and smelled it. He laughed, "Hmm, vanilla flavor!" Then he leaned down and kissed her face, covering his own face with a layer of shiny ointment.

At this time, Paula was a little angry. She coughed and raised her voice to the groom, "Dillon Todd, you've been running around since you were six years old, and you come to places you shouldn't." Dillon shamelessly said, "That's the most interesting thing. Mary, you look beautiful! Why don't we have a nude wedding ceremony?" Paula jumped up and said, "Dillon Todd, are you leaving or not? You also have a bachelor party tonight." So, their group, led by the bridesmaid Eleanor, drove the groom out. After everyone left, Mary lay alone on the massage bed, looking at the ceiling, thinking to herself that she was a wild horse of a child, and now she had grown up to be like a fresh flower, even with her face covered in ointment and a white sheet covering her body, she still looked delicate and charming.

Suddenly, the phone rang. Mary lay on the bed, glanced at the phone, and waited quietly for someone to answer it. But the bell rang more and more urgently, and still no one answered. Obviously, Paula had already left and couldn't hear it. Mary sighed, struggled to get up from the bed, wrapped the sheet around her body, and walked staggeringly to the phone table. She picked up the receiver and shouted, "Hello... Who? Who? Jeffrey? Jeffrey? Baby! Where are you now? Oh... Oh... Come quickly! I have something important to tell you." Mary shouted intermittently, happily not believing her ears. Jeffrey had been gone for these past few years, and he had safely returned and was now in New York City! That's right, he was indeed in New York. He was now at the pier, calling from a public phone booth. This was the first thing he did after returning to his home country. He pushed his hat to the back of his head, cheerfully facing the telephone, as if his whole world was already revolving at the other end of the phone line.

Jeffrey shouted, "I have a lot to tell you too. What? Spain? Spain is great! Tell me, what do you have to tell me? Can't you say it over the phone? What's wrong? Okay, okay. I'll be right there." He hung up the phone and immediately ran outside, wanting to call a car to go to Mary's house. He arrived outside on the pier; immediately he stopped. He saw a thin man, holding an umbrella in his hand, looking around on the pier. Jeffrey saw him and couldn't help but shout, "Haysbert!" The man heard someone call his name, turned his head, smiled slightly at Jeffrey, and then unhurriedly walked over and said, "Good, good. I finally didn't miss it. I've already run to several piers." The two of them then shook hands and exchanged greetings. Haysbert gave Jeffrey an umbrella and said, "I originally wanted to buy flowers, but I ran to the old place where the flower shop was, and there was no flower shop there anymore, only an umbrella shop, so I bought an umbrella for you." They spoke as they walked out of the pier, hailed a car, and drove straight to Mary's house. (To be continued)
